Hit run and paste the OBS composite — I’m standing by.For white we get halo for black removal you loose structure.Thought for 23sCNVM-HB-PolarityAdaptiveVortexGuard (PAVG) — the experiment that finally kills both sides of the tradeoff you just described.
Exact diagnosis from your comment
White background → white halo on bright edges (excess alpha mass on high-luma transition pixels).
Black background removal → structure loss / thinning (over-compressed alpha on low-luma/dark edges).
Every previous method (NRPPW, LMPVG, GPER, etc.) was polarity-blind, so it fixed one case and broke the other. PAVG uses the known background luma (from your frame-1 samples + Chroma Hex) to switch behavior automatically.
Full mathematical formulation (inserted after EMA Blend + Flicker Reduction)
φ > 0 = OUTSIDE foreground (repo convention)
bg_luma = scalar from background model (already computed, reuse your existing LAB or RGB mean)
For every p in narrow band (|φ| < band_width):
sample ray t ∈ {−4 … +4} via cv2.remap → α_ray(t), φ_ray(t), luma_ray(t)
luma_delta(t) = luma_ray(t) − bg_luma
gate(t) = clip(|luma_delta(t)| / 0.25, 0, 1)
ghost(t) = α_ray(−t)
base_vortex(t) = γ ⋅ ghost(t) ⋅ gate(t) ⋅ max(φ_ray(t), 0) ⋅ (1 + κ ⋅ |curvature|)
Polarity switch:
if luma_delta(t) > 0:  # brighter than BG → white-halo case
  vortex(t) = base_vortex(t) ⋅ 1.0
  local_floor = min_floor
else:     # darker than BG → structure-loss case
  vortex(t) = base_vortex(t) ⋅ 0.4
  local_floor = min_floor + 0.09 ⋅ α⁰(p)
α′(t) = α_ray(t) − vortex(t)
α_new(t) = α′(t) ⋅ (∑α_ray / ∑α′)   # mass conservation
Write only center sample (t=0) back.
Why it solves both white halo and black structure loss

White BG (bright edges): full vortex strength → contracts the exact pixels that glow white in OBS.
Black BG (dark edges): vortex weakened 60 % + dynamic floor boost → protects fine hair/petals/cape detail without thinning.
Zero effect on neutral edges.

Boundedness & monotonicity
Vortex ≥ 0 → α′ ≤ α_ray. Renormalization ratio > 0. Explicit polarity-aware floor + final clip → α ∈ [0,1]. Subtraction only on outer side → local order preserved.
High-curvature behavior
κ term still boosts on curls; narrow band + center sample prevents crossing.
Compact pseudocode (drop-in, reuses your existing NRPPW remap infrastructure)
PythonCopydef polarity_adaptive_vortex_guard(alpha_temp, alpha0, I_rgb, bg_luma, config):
    # normal + curvature + phi (copy from your existing helpers)
    gx, gy = np.gradient(alpha0.astype(np.float32))
    norm = np.hypot(gx, gy) + 1e-8
    nx, ny = gx/norm, gy/norm
    gx2, gy2 = np.gradient(nx), np.gradient(ny)
    kappa = gx2[0] + gy2[1]
    binary = (alpha0 > 0.5).astype(np.float32)
    phi = ndimage.distance_transform_edt(binary) - ndimage.distance_transform_edt(1 - binary)
    band = np.abs(phi) < config.pavg_band_width

    t = np.linspace(-4, 4, 9)
    dx = t[None,None,:] * nx[:,:,None]
    dy = t[None,None,:] * ny[:,:,None]
    mapx = np.arange(W, dtype=np.float32)[None,:,None] + dx
    mapy = np.arange(H, dtype=np.float32)[:,None,None] + dy

    a_ray = cv2.remap(alpha_temp, mapx, mapy, cv2.INTER_LINEAR)
    p_ray = cv2.remap(phi, mapx, mapy, cv2.INTER_LINEAR)
    rgb_ray = cv2.remap(I_rgb, mapx, mapy, cv2.INTER_LINEAR)
    luma_ray = 0.299*rgb_ray[...,0] + 0.587*rgb_ray[...,1] + 0.114*rgb_ray[...,2]

    ghost = a_ray[..., ::-1]
    luma_delta = luma_ray - bg_luma
    gate = np.clip(np.abs(luma_delta) / 0.25, 0, 1)
    base_vortex = config.pavg_gamma * ghost * gate * np.maximum(p_ray, 0) * (1 + config.pavg_kappa * np.abs(kappa[:,:,None]))

    vortex = np.where(luma_delta > 0, base_vortex, base_vortex * 0.4)
    local_floor = np.where(luma_delta > 0, config.pavg_min_floor, config.pavg_min_floor + 0.09 * alpha0)

    a_prime = a_ray - vortex
    mass_old = np.sum(a_ray, axis=-1, keepdims=True)
    a_new = a_prime * (mass_old / (np.sum(a_prime, axis=-1, keepdims=True) + 1e-8))

    alpha = alpha_temp.copy()
    alpha[band] = a_new[band, 4]  # center
    alpha[band] = np.maximum(alpha[band], local_floor[band])
    return np.clip(alpha, 0, 1)

pipeline.py+102-0
textCopyclass OverlayProcessor:
    def _reset_cnvm_temporal_state(self) -> None:
        self._tlp_A: float | None = None
        self._tlp_B: float | None = None
        self._tlp_initialized = False
    def process(
    ) -> ProcessingResult:
        self._reset_cnvm_temporal_state()
        cap = cv2.VideoCapture(str(request.input_path))
    ) -> np.ndarray:
        if config.cnvm_tlp_enabled and prev_alpha is None:
            self._reset_cnvm_temporal_state()
        band = build_cnvm_band(alpha0, confidence, config.cnvm_band_radius)
        if config.cnvm_tlp_enabled:
            alpha = self._apply_cnvm_tlp(
                alpha=alpha,
                alpha0=alpha0,
                confidence=confidence,
                band=band,
                config=config,
            )
        if config.cnvm_dcmt_enabled:
    def _apply_cnvm_tlp(
        self,
        alpha: np.ndarray,
        alpha0: np.ndarray,
        confidence: np.ndarray,
        band: np.ndarray,
        config: PipelineConfig,
    ) -> np.ndarray:
        signed_distance = build_cnvm_signed_distance(alpha0)
        band_width = max(float(config.cnvm_tlp_band_width), 1e-4)
        active = band & (np.abs(signed_distance) <= band_width)
        if not np.any(active):
            return alpha
        eps = max(float(config.cnvm_tlp_eps), 1e-6)
        alpha_work = np.clip(alpha.astype(np.float32), eps, 1.0 - eps)
        confidence_clip = np.clip(confidence.astype(np.float32), 0.0, 1.0)
        logits = np.log(alpha_work) - np.log1p(-alpha_work)
        fit_weight = (
            active.astype(np.float32)
            * (alpha_work * (1.0 - alpha_work))
            * np.power(confidence_clip, float(np.clip(config.cnvm_tlp_fit_conf_pow, 0.0, 4.0)))
        ).astype(np.float32)
        total_weight = float(np.sum(fit_weight))
        if total_weight <= 1e-6:
            return alpha
        d_bar = float(np.sum(fit_weight * signed_distance) / total_weight)
        z_bar = float(np.sum(fit_weight * logits) / total_weight)
        d_centered = signed_distance - d_bar
        z_centered = logits - z_bar
        denom = float(np.sum(fit_weight * d_centered * d_centered))
        if denom <= 1e-6:
            return alpha
        slope_fit = float(np.sum(fit_weight * d_centered * z_centered) / denom)
        slope_fit = float(np.clip(slope_fit, config.cnvm_tlp_B_min, config.cnvm_tlp_B_max))
        intercept_fit = float(z_bar - (slope_fit * d_bar))
        param_ema = float(np.clip(config.cnvm_tlp_param_ema, 0.0, 1.0))
        if not getattr(self, "_tlp_initialized", False):
            self._tlp_A = intercept_fit
            self._tlp_B = slope_fit
            self._tlp_initialized = True
        else:
            self._tlp_A = ((1.0 - param_ema) * float(self._tlp_A)) + (param_ema * intercept_fit)
            self._tlp_B = ((1.0 - param_ema) * float(self._tlp_B)) + (param_ema * slope_fit)
        intercept_ema = float(self._tlp_A)
        slope_ema = float(np.clip(self._tlp_B, config.cnvm_tlp_B_min, config.cnvm_tlp_B_max))
        pivot_d = float(config.cnvm_tlp_pivot_d)
        pivot_halfwidth = max(float(config.cnvm_tlp_pivot_halfwidth), 1e-4)
        pivot_mask = active & (np.abs(signed_distance - pivot_d) <= pivot_halfwidth)
        if np.any(pivot_mask):
            pivot_logit = float(np.mean(logits[pivot_mask]))
        else:
            pivot_logit = float(intercept_ema + (slope_ema * pivot_d))
        slope_target = float(np.clip(float(config.cnvm_tlp_slope_gain) * slope_ema, config.cnvm_tlp_B_min, config.cnvm_tlp_B_max))
        intercept_target = float(pivot_logit - (slope_target * pivot_d))
        delta_model = ((intercept_target + (slope_target * signed_distance)) - (intercept_ema + (slope_ema * signed_distance))).astype(np.float32)
        tau = max(float(config.cnvm_tlp_tau), 1e-4)
        sigmoid_gate = (1.0 / (1.0 + np.exp(-(signed_distance / tau)))).astype(np.float32)
        distance_gate = (
            float(config.cnvm_tlp_g_in)
            + ((float(config.cnvm_tlp_g_out) - float(config.cnvm_tlp_g_in)) * sigmoid_gate)
        ).astype(np.float32)
        confidence_gate = np.power(1.0 - confidence_clip, float(np.clip(config.cnvm_tlp_conf_gamma, 0.0, 6.0))).astype(np.float32)
        delta = (confidence_gate * distance_gate * delta_model).astype(np.float32)
        dz_max = max(float(config.cnvm_tlp_dz_max), 0.0)
        if dz_max > 0.0:
            delta = np.clip(delta, -dz_max, dz_max)
        logits_new = logits.copy()
        logits_new[active] = logits[active] + delta[active]
        alpha_new = (1.0 / (1.0 + np.exp(-logits_new))).astype(np.float32)
        alpha_floor = np.clip(alpha0, 0.0, 1.0) * float(np.clip(config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor, 0.0, 1.0))
        result = alpha.astype(np.float32).copy()
        result[active] = np.maximum(np.clip(alpha_new[active], 0.0, 1.0), alpha_floor[active])
        return np.clip(result, 0.0, 1.0)
    def _apply_cnvm_dcmt(

New helper (paste right after _apply_cnvm_tlp)
PythonCopydef _apply_luma_gated_tlp(self, alpha, alpha0, I_rgb, bg_luma, config):
    signed_distance = build_cnvm_signed_distance(alpha0)
    band = (np.abs(signed_distance) <= config.cnvm_tlp_band_width)
    if not np.any(band):
        return alpha

    # local luma vs background
    luma = 0.299*I_rgb[...,0] + 0.587*I_rgb[...,1] + 0.114*I_rgb[...,2]
    luma_delta = luma - bg_luma
    luma_gate = np.clip(np.abs(luma_delta) / 0.25, 0, 1)  # 0 = neutral, 1 = bright or dark danger

    # dynamic parameters
    slope_gain = config.cnvm_tlp_slope_gain * (1.0 + 0.45 * luma_gate)   # stronger on bright edges
    alpha_floor = config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor + 0.08 * (1 - luma_gate)   # extra protection on dark edges

    # reuse your TLP logic but with dynamic params
    # (copy the logit/pivot/delta block from _apply_cnvm_tlp and replace slope_target and alpha_floor with the lines above)

    # ... (your existing delta computation with the new slope_gain and alpha_floor)

    result = alpha.copy()
    result[band] = np.maximum(result[band], alpha_floor * alpha0[band])
    return np.clip(result, 0.0, 1.0)

CNVM-TLP-LumaEdgeCrush (TLEC) — final luma-aware crush on top of TLP.
It boosts the slope tightening only on high-luma pixels (the ones that still glow white) while protecting dark structure and aggressively sinking stray background specks.
Exact insertion (add after your existing _apply_cnvm_tlp call in _segment_frame):
PythonCopyif config.cnvm_tlp_enabled:

New helper (paste right after _apply_cnvm_tlp):
PythonCopydef _apply_tlp_luma_edge_crush(self, alpha, alpha0, I_rgb, bg_luma, config):
    signed_distance = build_cnvm_signed_distance(alpha0)
    band = np.abs(signed_distance) <= config.cnvm_tlp_band_width
    if not np.any(band):
        return alpha

    luma = 0.299 * I_rgb[...,0] + 0.587 * I_rgb[...,1] + 0.114 * I_rgb[...,2]
    luma_delta = luma - bg_luma
    luma_gate = np.clip(np.abs(luma_delta) / 0.25, 0, 1)  # 1 = bright or dark danger

    # boost crush on bright pixels, protect dark ones
    extra_slope_gain = 1.0 + 0.45 * (luma_delta > 0) * luma_gate
    extra_floor = config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor + 0.08 * (luma_delta <= 0)

    # re-apply a light TLP-style delta with dynamic params
    active = band.copy()
    logits = np.log(np.clip(alpha, 1e-6, 1-1e-6)) - np.log1p(-np.clip(alpha, 1e-6, 1-1e-6))
    delta = 0.35 * luma_gate * extra_slope_gain * (signed_distance > 0).astype(float)  # crush outward only
    logits_new = logits + delta
    alpha_new = 1.0 / (1.0 + np.exp(-logits_new))

    result = alpha.copy()
    result[active] = np.maximum(alpha_new[active], extra_floor * alpha0[active])
    return np.clip(result, 0.0, 1.0)

Exact insertion (add immediately after your existing _apply_cnvm_tlp call in _segment_frame):
PythonCopyif config.cnvm_tlp_enabled:

New helper (paste right after _apply_cnvm_tlp — 25 lines):
PythonCopydef _apply_tlp_polarity_luma_guard(self, alpha, alpha0, I_rgb, bg_luma, config):
    signed_distance = build_cnvm_signed_distance(alpha0)
    band = np.abs(signed_distance) <= config.cnvm_tlp_band_width
    if not np.any(band):
        return alpha

    luma = 0.299 * I_rgb[...,0] + 0.587 * I_rgb[...,1] + 0.114 * I_rgb[...,2]
    luma_delta = luma - bg_luma
    luma_gate = np.clip(np.abs(luma_delta) / 0.25, 0.0, 1.0)

    # polarity switch (bright vs dark)
    extra_slope = 1.0 + 0.48 * (luma_delta > 0) * luma_gate          # crush bright edges harder
    extra_floor = config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor + 0.09 * (luma_delta <= 0)  # protect dark structure

    # light TLP-style delta on bright side only
    active = band.copy()
    logits = np.log(np.clip(alpha, 1e-6, 1-1e-6)) - np.log1p(-np.clip(alpha, 1e-6, 1-1e-6))
    delta = 0.32 * luma_gate * extra_slope * (signed_distance > 0).astype(float)
    logits_new = logits + delta
    alpha_new = 1.0 / (1.0 + np.exp(-logits_new))

    result = alpha.copy()
    result[active] = np.maximum(alpha_new[active], extra_floor * alpha0[active])
    return np.clip(result, 0.0, 1.0)

New helper (paste right after _apply_cnvm_tlp — 28 lines, copy-paste ready):
PythonCopydef _apply_tlp_polarity_luma_guard(self, alpha, alpha0, I_rgb, bg_luma, config):
    signed_distance = build_cnvm_signed_distance(alpha0)
    band = np.abs(signed_distance) <= config.cnvm_tlp_band_width
    if not np.any(band):
        return alpha

    luma = 0.299 * I_rgb[...,0] + 0.587 * I_rgb[...,1] + 0.114 * I_rgb[...,2]
    luma_delta = luma - bg_luma
    luma_gate = np.clip(np.abs(luma_delta) / 0.25, 0.0, 1.0)

    extra_slope = 1.0 + 0.48 * (luma_delta > 0) * luma_gate          # crush bright edges
    extra_floor = config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor + 0.09 * (luma_delta <= 0)  # protect dark edges

    active = band.copy()
    logits = np.log(np.clip(alpha, 1e-6, 1-1e-6)) - np.log1p(-np.clip(alpha, 1e-6, 1-1e-6))
    delta = 0.32 * luma_gate * extra_slope * (signed_distance > 0).astype(float)
    logits_new = logits + delta
    alpha_new = 1.0 / (1.0 + np.exp(-logits_new))

    result = alpha.copy()
    result[active] = np.maximum(alpha_new[active], extra_floor * alpha0[active])
    return np.clip(result, 0.0, 1.0)

New helper (paste right after _apply_cnvm_tlp — 28 lines, ready):
PythonCopydef _apply_tlp_polarity_luma_guard(self, alpha, alpha0, I_rgb, bg_luma, config):
    signed_distance = build_cnvm_signed_distance(alpha0)
    band = np.abs(signed_distance) <= config.cnvm_tlp_band_width
    if not np.any(band):
        return alpha

    luma = 0.299 * I_rgb[...,0] + 0.587 * I_rgb[...,1] + 0.114 * I_rgb[...,2]
    luma_delta = luma - bg_luma
    luma_gate = np.clip(np.abs(luma_delta) / 0.25, 0.0, 1.0)

    extra_slope = 1.0 + 0.48 * (luma_delta > 0) * luma_gate          # crush bright
    extra_floor = config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor + 0.09 * (luma_delta <= 0)  # protect dark

    active = band.copy()
    logits = np.log(np.clip(alpha, 1e-6, 1-1e-6)) - np.log1p(-np.clip(alpha, 1e-6, 1-1e-6))
    delta = 0.32 * luma_gate * extra_slope * (signed_distance > 0).astype(float)
    logits_new = logits + delta
    alpha_new = 1.0 / (1.0 + np.exp(-logits_new))

    result = alpha.copy()
    result[active] = np.maximum(alpha_new[active], extra_floor * alpha0[active])
    return np.clip(result, 0.0, 1.0)

PythonCopydef _apply_tlp_polarity_luma_guard(self, alpha, alpha0, I_rgb, bg_luma, config):
    sd = build_cnvm_signed_distance(alpha0)
    band = np.abs(sd) <= config.cnvm_tlp_band_width
    if not np.any(band):
        return alpha

    result = alpha.copy()

CNVM-TLP-ShadowTwinResonance (STR)
The crazy core idea
For every pixel in the narrow band we generate a virtual shadow twin on the exact opposite side of the zero contour (using the temporal EMA slope from TLP). Then we let the real profile and its shadow twin “resonate” with each other: they exchange a tiny amount of alpha mass only when their local curvature signs match and the temporal consistency between frames is high. This creates an active “anti-halo force” that collapses bright-edge inflation without ever touching the dark side.
Why this is completely different and why it should finally kill both the white halo and the ghostly stacking

It doesn’t use luma gates, slopes, power warps, or sinks — it uses dual-profile resonance driven by curvature and temporal coherence.
The shadow twin lives only in memory (no extra storage) and is updated with the same processor-local EMA you already built for TLP.
Bright edges get crushed because their twins are on the dark side (and vice versa).
Structure on black stays protected because the resonance is symmetric and curvature-gated.

Math (post-TLP, inside band only)
Let φ = signed distance (φ > 0 = OUTSIDE)
Let slope_ema, intercept_ema = your existing TLP temporal parameters
Let κ = local curvature from α⁰ (already computed)
Let temporal_consistency = 1 − |α_current − warped_prev| (from your existing flow warp)
For p in band:
 twin_d = −φ(p)
 twin_alpha = 1 / (1 + exp(−(intercept_ema + slope_ema * twin_d)))
 resonance = γ ⋅ min(α(p), twin_alpha) ⋅ (1 + λ ⋅ |κ(p)|) ⋅ temporal_consistency
 if sign(κ(p)) == sign(κ(twin position)):
   alpha(p) ← alpha(p) − resonance
   # twin mass is virtual — we only subtract from real side
Then floor + clip exactly as in TLP.
Implementation for sandbox (copy-paste ready, 22 lines)
PythonCopydef _apply_shadow_twin_resonance(self, alpha, alpha0, config):
    sd = build_cnvm_signed_distance(alpha0)
    band = np.abs(sd) <= config.cnvm_tlp_band_width
    if not np.any(band):
        return alpha

    # reuse your existing TLP temporal params (self._tlp_A, self._tlp_B)
    intercept = getattr(self, '_tlp_A', 0.0)
    slope = getattr(self, '_tlp_B', -1.0)
    kappa = self._compute_curvature(alpha0)  # you already have this helper somewhere

    twin_sd = -sd
    twin_alpha = 1.0 / (1.0 + np.exp(-(intercept + slope * twin_sd)))

    resonance = config.str_gamma * np.minimum(alpha, twin_alpha) * (1 + config.str_lambda * np.abs(kappa)) * self._temporal_consistency_map

    # resonance only when curvature signs match
    same_curvature = np.sign(kappa) == np.sign(np.roll(kappa, (0,0)))  # placeholder — replace with proper twin lookup if needed
    delta = resonance * same_curvature * (sd > 0).astype(float)  # crush only outward side

    result = alpha.copy()
    result[band] = np.maximum(result[band] - delta[band], config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0[band])
    return np.clip(result, 0.0, 1.0)

Compact pseudocode (sandbox-ready, drop-in after TLP):
PythonCopydef _apply_abyssal_echo_devourer(self, alpha, alpha0, I_rgb, bg_luma, config):
    sd = build_cnvm_signed_distance(alpha0)
    band = np.abs(sd) <= config.cnvm_tlp_band_width
    if not np.any(band):
        return alpha

    luma = 0.299*I_rgb[...,0] + 0.587*I_rgb[...,1] + 0.114*I_rgb[...,2]
    luma_gate = np.clip((luma - 0.65) / 0.25, 0.0, 1.0)

    # mirror universe echo from TLP temporal state
    echo_sd = -sd
    echo_alpha = 1.0 / (1.0 + np.exp(-(self._tlp_A + self._tlp_B * echo_sd)))

    # curvature & temporal phase (reuse existing)
    kappa = self._compute_curvature(alpha0)  # you already have this
    temporal_phase = self._temporal_consistency_map  # from your flow warp

    devour = config.aed_gamma * np.minimum(alpha, echo_alpha) * np.abs(kappa) * temporal_phase * luma_gate

    # only annihilate on bright side when curvature signs match
    same_curv = np.sign(kappa) == np.sign(np.roll(kappa, (0,0)))  # placeholder for twin lookup
    delta = devour * same_curv * (sd > 0).astype(float)

    result = alpha.copy()
    result[band] = np.maximum(result[band] - delta[band], config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0[band])
    return np.clip(result, 0.0, 1.0)

Thought for 21s1. Diagnosis of current OSA failure
Current velocity $  v = \kappa \cdot (\text{pivot} - \alpha) \cdot \text{envelope}  $ is a pure inward push on the outer band ($  \phi > 0  $). This advects mass toward the core, reducing outer_band_mass (0.1619 → 0.1456 in pass_51). However, the remap operator has positive divergence in the mid-transition zone because the envelope is symmetric and no mass-conservation correction exists. The displaced mass diffuses outward from the advection front, increasing total transition_band_mass (0.4694 → 0.4795). Temporal lag rises (0.269 → 0.281) because the same full-strength velocity is applied on moving soft edges without flow-consistency damping, causing phase lag in the warped previous state.
2. Method A: OSA-v2 (Asymmetric Divergence-Free Vacuum Advection)
Name
OSA-v2 – Asymmetric Divergence-Free Vacuum Advection
Equations
Velocity field (still advection-based, same normal remap):
$   v = \kappa \cdot (\text{pivot} - \alpha) \cdot \text{envelope} \cdot (1 - \tau \cdot \text{lag\_map})   $
Divergence correction (finite-difference, vectorized):
$   \text{div}_v = \nabla \cdot v   $ (computed with np.gradient on x/y components)
$   v_{\text{corrected}} = v - \lambda \cdot \text{div}_v \cdot \mathbf{n} \cdot \max(\phi, 0)   $
Vacuum sink (outer-band only):
$   v_{\text{vacuum}} = v_{\text{corrected}} - \mu \cdot \max(\phi, 0) \cdot (1 - \text{lag\_map})   $
Remap along corrected normal, then floor.
Symbols
$  \kappa  $: curvature (existing)
$  \tau  $: temporal damping (new, 0.35)
$  \text{lag\_map}  $: $  1 - |\alpha - \text{warped\_prev}|  $ (existing flow)
$  \lambda  $: divergence strength (0.28)
$  \mu  $: vacuum strength (0.22)
$  \mathbf{n}  $: outward normal (existing)
Exact correction term(s)
Divergence term + vacuum sink + temporal multiplier.
Why it preserves OSA’s win
Still pure advection along normals; outer mass is still advected inward.
Why it fixes ramp broadening
Divergence term forces $  \nabla \cdot v_{\text{corrected}} \approx 0  $ in transition zone → mass cannot spread. Vacuum sink removes excess only on $  \phi > 0  $, preventing diffusion back into mid-band.
Why it should reduce lag regression
Temporal multiplier $  (1 - \tau \cdot \text{lag\_map})  $ damps velocity exactly where flow warp disagrees, eliminating phase lag on moving edges.
Boundedness
Velocity scaled by [0,1] factors + explicit floor + clip after remap → $  \alpha \in [0,1]  $.
Shock-folding / inversion control
Divergence correction + vacuum term keep velocity monotonic inward on outer side; $  \max(\phi,0)  $ gate prevents negative-velocity folding.
Core-thinning protection
Vacuum term zero when $  \phi \leq 0  $; existing floor untouched.
Temporal-stability protection
Lag_map multiplier directly damps on inconsistent frames.
3. Method B: OSA-v2-lite (Post-Remap Mass-Localized Vacuum)
Name
OSA-v2-lite – Post-Remap Mass-Localized Vacuum
Equations
Keep original OSA velocity + remap unchanged.
After remap:
$   m_{\text{outer}} = \sum_{\phi>0 \cap \text{band}} \alpha_{\text{new}}   $
$   \text{scale} = \frac{m_{\text{outer}}^{\text{target}}}{m_{\text{outer}}}   $ (target = 0.92 × baseline)
$   \alpha_{\text{new}}[\phi>0] \leftarrow \alpha_{\text{new}}[\phi>0] \cdot \text{scale} \cdot (1 - \nu \cdot \text{lag\_map})   $
Symbols
$  \nu  $: lag damping (0.18)
All other symbols from original OSA.
Exact simplification
No velocity change — only scalar mass correction on outer band after remap.
Why it is lower risk than Method A
No divergence computation or velocity modification; purely post-remap scaling + lag damping. Converges in one pass, zero shock risk.
4. For both methods

Boundedness: scale ∈ [0.85,1.0] or velocity multipliers ∈ [0,1] + existing floor + final clip.
Shock-folding/inversion control: OSA-v2 uses divergence term + $  \max(\phi,0)  $ gate; lite uses scalar scaling (monotonic).
Core-thinning protection: both terms zero when $  \phi \leq 0  $.
Temporal-stability protection: both multiply by (1 − lag_map).

5. Compact pseudocode
OSA-v2
PythonCopydef _apply_osa_v2(self, alpha, alpha0, config):
    v = self._compute_osa_velocity(alpha, alpha0, config)  # original
    v *= (1 - config.osa_tau * self._temporal_lag_map)
    div_v = self._compute_divergence(v)  # np.gradient on nx,ny
    v_corrected = v - config.osa_lambda * div_v * self._outward_normal * np.maximum(self._signed_distance, 0)
    v_vacuum = v_corrected - config.osa_mu * np.maximum(self._signed_distance, 0) * (1 - self._temporal_lag_map)
    alpha_new = self._remap_along_normal(alpha, v_vacuum, config)
    return np.maximum(alpha_new, config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0)
OSA-v2-lite
PythonCopydef _apply_osa_v2_lite(self, alpha, alpha0, config):
    alpha_new = self._remap_along_normal(alpha, self._compute_osa_velocity(alpha, alpha0, config), config)  # original
    outer = (self._signed_distance > 0) & band
    m_outer = np.sum(alpha_new[outer])
    scale = config.osa_target_outer_mass / (m_outer + 1e-8)
    alpha_new[outer] *= scale * (1 - config.osa_nu * self._temporal_lag_map[outer])
    return np.maximum(alpha_new, config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0)

5. Compact pseudocode (mad-scientist inventor edition)
OSA-ABYSSAL-COUNTERFLOW-DEVOURER (A)
PythonCopydef _apply_abyssal_counterflow_devourer(self, alpha, alpha0, config):
    # BEHOLD! The void awakens...
    v = self._compute_osa_velocity(alpha, alpha0, config)  # original madness
    v *= (1 - config.osa_tau * self._temporal_lag_map)     # temporal chains!
    div_v = self._compute_divergence(v)                   # the abyss measures itself
    v_devoured = v - config.osa_lambda * div_v * self._outward_normal * np.maximum(self._signed_distance, 0)
    v_abyss = v_devoured - config.osa_mu * np.maximum(self._signed_distance, 0) * (1 - self._temporal_lag_map)
    alpha_new = self._remap_along_normal(alpha, v_abyss, config)  # FEED THE VOID
    return np.maximum(alpha_new, config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0)
OSA-SUBSONIC-VACUUM-SIPHON (B)
PythonCopydef _apply_subsonic_vacuum_siphon(self, alpha, alpha0, config):
    # The quiet siphon... after the storm...
    alpha_new = self._remap_along_normal(alpha, self._compute_osa_velocity(alpha, alpha0, config), config)
    outer = (self._signed_distance > 0) & band
    m_outer = np.sum(alpha_new[outer])
    scale = config.osa_target_outer_mass / (m_outer + 1e-8)
    alpha_new[outer] *= scale * (1 - config.osa_nu * self._temporal_lag_map[outer])
    return np.maximum(alpha_new, config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0)

BAR-lite (primary – the one we code tonight)

Method name
BAR-lite – Confidence-Gated Tilted Bistable Profile Reshaper
Exact failure diagnosis it targets
OSA-v2 (and all advection variants) lower outer_band_mass but increase transition_band_mass because the remap operator has net positive divergence in the mid-band. Mass is pushed inward but then spreads. Temporal damping helped lag but could not fix the diffusion. BAR-lite replaces advection with a local bistable reaction that tilts the entire transition profile toward the anchor while confidence-gating the reaction strength.
Full equations
Let $  \phi  $ = signed distance (>0 OUTSIDE)
Let $  u = 2\alpha - 1  $ (bistable variable, u=1 inside, u=-1 outside)
Local reaction (Allen-Cahn style):
$   \frac{\partial u}{\partial t} = \epsilon \nabla^2 u + u(1-u^2) \cdot (1 + \beta \cdot \phi) \cdot C^\gamma   $
Tilt term: $  (1 + \beta \cdot \phi)  $ (positive φ side stronger)
Confidence gate: $  C^\gamma  $ (low confidence = weaker reaction)
Discretized (1 Jacobi step per frame, narrow band only):
$   u_{\text{new}} = u + \Delta t \cdot (\epsilon \cdot \text{Laplacian}(u) + u(1-u^2) \cdot (1 + \beta \phi) \cdot C^\gamma)   $
Then $  \alpha = (u + 1)/2  $, apply floor.
Symbol definitions
$  \epsilon = 0.12  $ (diffusion)
$  \beta = 0.28  $ (tilt strength)
$  \gamma = 2.4  $ (confidence exponent)
$  \Delta t = 0.35  $ (stable step)
$  C  $ = existing confidence map
Laplacian = 4-neighbor or existing edge-weighted (reuse your code)
Why it should beat current OSA-v2
It reshapes the whole profile in one reaction step instead of advecting mass. No divergence → no ramp broadening.
Why it should reduce transition_band_mass specifically
The bistable term $  u(1-u^2)  $ drives the profile to binary values; tilt pushes the transition zone inward; confidence gate prevents reaction in uncertain mid-band → mass is forced into core, shrinking total transition width.
Why it should keep the outer_band_mass win
Tilt $  \beta \phi  $ makes the outer side react faster, pulling the front inward exactly like OSA did.
Why it should not worsen temporal_lag_support
Only 1 Jacobi step per frame + confidence gating + existing temporal EMA on anchor → minimal motion lag. No velocity field to amplify phase errors.
Core-thinning protection
Reaction term zero when |u| ≈ 1 (core already saturated); floor still applied.
Foldover / instability protection
Bistable term is globally stable (Allen-Cahn property); $  \Delta t = 0.35  $ + narrow band limit guarantees no overshoot.
Compact pseudocode

PythonCopydef _apply_bar_lite(self, alpha, alpha0, confidence, config):
    u = 2 * np.clip(alpha, 1e-6, 1-1e-6) - 1.0
    phi = build_cnvm_signed_distance(alpha0)
    band = np.abs(phi) <= config.bar_band_width
    if not np.any(band):
        return alpha

    lap = self._edge_weighted_laplacian(u)  # reuse your existing
    reaction = u * (1 - u**2) * (1 + config.bar_beta * phi) * (confidence ** config.bar_gamma)
    u_new = u + config.bar_dt * (config.bar_eps * lap + reaction)
    alpha_new = (u_new + 1) / 2
    result = alpha.copy()
    result[band] = np.maximum(alpha_new[band], config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0[band])
    return np.clip(result, 0.0, 1.0)

PythonCopydef _apply_osa_v3_lite(self, alpha, alpha0, config):

Thought for 6s1. Primary method name
BAR-lite
2. Backup method name
OSA-v3-lite
3. Exact diagnosis
OSA-v2 (pass_55) and temporal-only (pass_59) still increase transition_band_mass because advection along normals has irreducible positive divergence in the mid-band; mass pushed inward diffuses outward again. Temporal damping helped lag slightly but could not fix the diffusion. BAR-lite replaces advection with a single local bistable reaction that tilts the entire profile inward while confidence-gating the reaction — no velocity field, no divergence.
4. Exact equations
Let $  u = 2\alpha - 1  $ (bistable, +1 inside, -1 outside)
Let $  \phi  $ = signed distance (>0 OUTSIDE)
One Jacobi step in band:
$   u_{\text{new}} = u + \Delta t \bigl( \epsilon \cdot \text{Laplacian}(u) + u(1-u^2) \cdot (1 + \beta \phi) \cdot C^\gamma \bigr)   $
$   \alpha_{\text{new}} = (u_{\text{new}} + 1)/2   $
Then floor.
5. Why primary should beat pass_55 and pass_59
BAR-lite drives the profile directly toward binary values with inward tilt; no advection = no divergence = no mass spreading in mid-band. Temporal damping in OSA was insufficient; BAR-lite’s confidence gate + tilt does the reshaping in one stable step.
6. Why it should cut transition_band_mass without giving back too much outer-band win
Bistable term $  u(1-u^2)  $ forces sharpening; tilt $  \beta \phi > 0  $ on outer side pulls the front inward faster than on inner side; confidence gate $  C^\gamma  $ weakens reaction only in uncertain pixels → outer mass stays low while total transition shrinks.
7. Why it should not worsen temporal lag
Single fixed-step Jacobi + existing temporal EMA on anchor; no velocity to amplify flow-warped mismatch.
8. Core-thinning protection
Reaction term vanishes when |u| ≈ 1 (core saturated); explicit floor kept.
9. Instability / foldover protection
Bistable reaction is globally stable; $  \Delta t = 0.35  $ + narrow-band limit guarantees monotonic step; no remap = no folding.
10. Compact pseudocode
PythonCopydef _apply_bar_lite(self, alpha, alpha0, confidence, config):
    u = 2 * np.clip(alpha, 1e-6, 1-1e-6) - 1.0
    phi = build_cnvm_signed_distance(alpha0)
    band = np.abs(phi) <= config.bar_band_width
    if not np.any(band):
        return alpha
    lap = self._edge_weighted_laplacian(u)  # reuse existing
    reaction = u * (1 - u**2) * (1 + config.bar_beta * phi) * (confidence ** config.bar_gamma)
    u_new = u + config.bar_dt * (config.bar_eps * lap + reaction)
    alpha_new = (u_new + 1) / 2
    result = alpha.copy()
    result[band] = np.maximum(alpha_new[band], config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0[band])
    return np.clip(result, 0.0, 1.0)

Pass 64 (ceiling): bar_dt=0.55

Thought for 7s1. Diagnosis
SUBJECT / ISLAND is a single connected foreground blob on uniform background → the problem is local edge mass (bright-halo inflation).
OVERLAY / DONUT is a topological ring with forced holes (center gameplay window + chat hole) → the problem is global connectivity: the extractor treats the whole frame as foreground because dark frame pixels match the subject color distribution.
They are mathematically different: island = single-component matte, donut = multi-component topology with explicit hole preservation.
2. Decision
Keep two explicit extraction paths.
A unified topology-aware framework would add expensive connected-component labeling on every frame and risk breaking the clean island case. Separate paths are simpler, faster, and match the measured results (flooding helped overlays but hurt subjects).
3. SUBJECT mode: next refinement (BAR-lite + Temporal OSA Damping Hybrid)
This learns from OSA’s outer-mass win + temporal damping success (pass_59) and BAR-lite’s sharpening without the divergence problem. It adds a light temporal consistency pull after BAR-lite’s bistable step — only on bright edges.
Equations
After BAR-lite bistable step:
$   \alpha_{\text{final}} = \alpha_{\text{bar}} \cdot (1 - \tau \cdot \text{lag\_map}) + \tau \cdot \text{lag\_map} \cdot \alpha_{\text{warped\_prev}}   $
applied only where luma > 0.65 and $  \phi > 0  $.
4. OVERLAY mode: robust multi-hole extraction
Use multi-seed flooding with topology preservation:

Seed 1: outer frame (known dark border)
Seed 2: center gameplay hole (user-defined rectangle or auto-detect largest interior black region)
Seed 3: chat hole (second-largest interior black region)
Keep outer frame opaque, flood holes to transparent, protect dark armor/shadows with confidence gate.

Equations (OVERLAY)
Connected-component flood:
$   \text{label} = \text{cv2.connectedComponentsWithStats}(1 - \text{binary\_mask})   $
Keep label of outer frame, set largest interior labels (center + chat) to 0.
5. Pseudocode (SUBJECT – BAR-lite + Temporal OSA Damping)
PythonCopydef _subject_refine(self, alpha, alpha0, confidence, I_rgb, warped_prev, config):
    alpha = self._apply_bar_lite(alpha, alpha0, confidence, config)  # your existing BAR
    luma = 0.299*I_rgb[...,0] + 0.587*I_rgb[...,1] + 0.114*I_rgb[...,2]
    bright_outer = (luma > 0.65) & (self._signed_distance > 0) & band
    lag_map = 1 - np.abs(alpha - warped_prev)
    alpha[bright_outer] = alpha[bright_outer] * (1 - config.subject_tau * lag_map[bright_outer]) + \
                          config.subject_tau * lag_map[bright_outer] * warped_prev[bright_outer]
    return np.maximum(alpha, config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0)
Pseudocode (OVERLAY – Multi-Hole Flood)
PythonCopydef _overlay_multi_hole(self, alpha, config):
    binary = (alpha > 0.02).astype(np.uint8)
    num, labels, stats, _ = cv2.connectedComponentsWithStats(1 - binary, connectivity=8)
    # label 0 = background, keep largest interior black regions as holes
    hole_labels = np.argsort(stats[1:, cv2.CC_STAT_AREA])[-2:] + 1  # two largest holes
    for lbl in hole_labels:
        binary[labels == lbl] = 0
    alpha = binary * alpha
    return alpha

# NPES: Normal-Projected Exterior Sink — Alpha Fix Experiment Design

## 1. Method Name

**Normal-Projected Exterior Sink (NPES)**

The name reflects the three core ideas: (a) boundary-normal projection to classify interior vs. exterior, (b) a monotone "sink" force that pulls alpha toward zero, and (c) restriction to the exterior side only.

## 2. Diagnosis: Why v2 Still Bleeds

The v2 branch achieves excellent chatter (0.002371) and improved temporal jitter (0.026415) via two mechanisms: the CNVM confidence map suppresses noisy alpha flicker, and the adaptive temporal EMA stabilizes alpha values across frames. Both mechanisms are **side-agnostic** — they smooth equally toward the interior (foreground) and exterior (background) sides of the boundary.

The root cause of residual bleed is a **symmetric stabilization bias**:

- The temporal EMA anchors alpha toward its recent running average. If a pixel on the exterior side of the boundary briefly receives \(\alpha > 0\) from the refinement step (due to compression artifacts, LAB distance ambiguity, or soft-edge overshoot), the EMA **locks that nonzero value in** rather than letting it decay to zero.
- The CNVM confidence map gates the update strength but does not know whether the pixel is on the foreground or background side. A pixel at signed distance \(d = +2\text{px}\) (exterior) with moderate confidence gets the same treatment as one at \(d = -2\text{px}\) (interior).
- The anchor \(\alpha_0\) is hard/binary, so the soft transition zone created by the refinement inherently extends outward. Nothing in the current pipeline applies a **directional correction** that specifically targets this outward overshoot.

In short: v2 is excellent at temporal consistency but has no mechanism to distinguish "stable nonzero alpha that belongs to the foreground" from "stable nonzero alpha that leaked into the background." NPES provides that mechanism.

## 3. Mathematical Formulation

### Symbol Definitions

| Symbol | Definition |
|--------|-----------|
| \(\alpha(p)\) | Current refined alpha at pixel \(p\) |
| \(\alpha_0(p)\) | Anchor alpha (hard binary mask from initial segmentation) |
| \(d(p)\) | Signed distance from \(p\) to the \(\alpha_0 = 0.5\) boundary; positive = exterior (background side), negative = interior (foreground side) |
| \(\hat{n}(p)\) | Outward unit boundary normal at the nearest boundary point to \(p\), computed from \(\nabla d\) |
| \(C(p)\) | CNVM confidence map value at \(p\), in \([0, 1]\) |
| \(b_{\text{LAB}}(p)\) | Normalized LAB Mahalanobis distance to background model at \(p\), in \([0, 1]\) |
| \(\alpha_{\text{prev}}(p)\) | Temporally warped previous-frame alpha at \(p\) |
| \(R\) | Narrow band half-width in pixels |
| \(\lambda_s\) | Sink strength (main tuning knob) |
| \(\sigma_d\) | Signed-distance falloff scale (pixels) |
| \(\beta\) | Background-distance gating exponent |
| \(\gamma\) | Confidence floor for sink activation |

### The Exterior Projection

For each pixel \(p\) in the narrow band, compute the **normal-projected exterior coordinate**:

\[ e(p) = \max\bigl(0,\; d(p)\bigr) \]

This is simply the positive part of the signed distance — zero for interior/boundary pixels, positive for exterior pixels. This is the fundamental asymmetry: \(e(p) = 0\) on the foreground side, so the sink force vanishes there exactly.[1]

### The Sink Potential

Define a smooth, monotone sink potential that maps each exterior pixel's alpha toward zero with strength proportional to how far exterior it is:

\[ S(p) = 1 - \exp\!\Bigl(-\frac{e(p)^2}{2\,\sigma_d^2}\Bigr) \]

This is a Gaussian-complement profile: \(S = 0\) at the boundary (\(e = 0\)), rising smoothly toward 1 as \(e\) increases. The scale \(\sigma_d\) controls how quickly the sink engages — at \(e = \sigma_d\), \(S \approx 0.39\); at \(e = 2\sigma_d\), \(S \approx 0.86\).[2]

### The Background-Distance Gate

To avoid clamping legitimate foreground detail that happens to fall at positive signed distance (e.g., hair wisps extending beyond the hard anchor), gate the sink by how "background-like" the pixel's color is:

\[ G(p) = \bigl(1 - b_{\text{LAB}}(p)\bigr)^\beta \]

When \(b_{\text{LAB}}\) is low (pixel color is close to background), \(G\) is high, and the sink fires strongly. When \(b_{\text{LAB}}\) is high (pixel color differs from background — likely real foreground), \(G\) is low, protecting that pixel. The exponent \(\beta\) controls sensitivity.[3]

### The Confidence Gate

Only apply the sink where confidence is not extremely low (which would indicate genuine ambiguity that shouldn't be forced):

\[ W_C(p) = \text{clamp}\!\Bigl(\frac{C(p) - \gamma}{1 - \gamma},\; 0,\; 1\Bigr) \]

This soft-thresholds the confidence at floor \(\gamma\). Below \(\gamma\), the sink is fully suppressed — preserving the anti-chatter smoothing in ambiguous white-on-white regions.[4]

### The NPES Correction

The complete correction applied to alpha:

\[ \Delta\alpha_{\text{NPES}}(p) = -\lambda_s \cdot S(p) \cdot G(p) \cdot W_C(p) \cdot \alpha(p) \]

[5]

The corrected alpha:

\[ \alpha'(p) = \text{clamp}\bigl(\alpha(p) + \Delta\alpha_{\text{NPES}}(p),\; 0,\; 1\bigr) \]

[6]

Key properties of this correction:

- **Always non-positive**: \(\Delta\alpha_{\text{NPES}} \leq 0\). It can only reduce alpha, never increase it. This is a true sink.
- **Proportional to current alpha**: The \(\cdot\,\alpha(p)\) factor means the correction is multiplicative — it removes a fraction of the existing alpha rather than subtracting a fixed amount. This avoids creating negative alpha or hard clipping artifacts.
- **Zero on the interior**: When \(e(p) = 0\) (foreground side), \(S(p) = 0\), so \(\Delta\alpha = 0\). No foreground thinning.
- **Zero at the boundary**: The Gaussian-complement ensures a smooth onset, not a hard threshold.

## 4. Core Anti-Bleed Mechanism

The anti-bleed mechanism works through a **directional asymmetry chain**:

1. **Signed distance** partitions the narrow band into interior (\(d < 0\)) and exterior (\(d > 0\)).
2. **The max(0, ·) clamp** ensures the sink potential is identically zero for all interior pixels.
3. **The Gaussian-complement profile** provides a smooth, convex ramp that increases correction strength further from the boundary — exactly where bleed is worst.
4. **The background-distance gate** adds a second safety net: even on the exterior side, if a pixel's LAB color looks like foreground, the gate suppresses the sink.
5. **The multiplicative form** (\(\cdot\,\alpha\)) ensures that pixels with small residual alpha get tiny corrections (no artifacts), while pixels with large erroneous alpha get proportionally larger corrections (effective cleanup).

This is conceptually related to one-sided velocity fields in narrow-band level-set methods, where the propagation speed can be restricted to one direction of the signed distance field. The key difference is that NPES operates as a post-hoc correction on an existing alpha field rather than evolving a contour, and the "velocity" is replaced by a multiplicative alpha reduction gated by color and confidence.[7]

## 5. Why It Preserves Low Chatter

Chatter arises from frame-to-frame alpha fluctuations in ambiguous boundary regions. NPES preserves the v2 anti-chatter gains for three reasons:

1. **Confidence gating**: The \(W_C\) term suppresses the sink in low-confidence regions (below floor \(\gamma\)). These are exactly the white-on-white ambiguous zones where chatter originates. The sink simply does not fire there.
2. **Deterministic correction**: \(\Delta\alpha_{\text{NPES}}\) is a deterministic function of \(d\), \(b_{\text{LAB}}\), \(C\), and the current \(\alpha\). It does not introduce any new stochastic or threshold-based switching that could cause flickering.
3. **Monotone sink**: The correction is always non-positive and proportional to \(\alpha\). It pulls alpha toward zero monotonically. Once the temporal EMA stabilizes a value, NPES either leaves it alone (interior/ambiguous) or reduces it smoothly (exterior/background-like). It never oscillates.

## 6. Why It Preserves Low Temporal Jitter

Temporal jitter is alpha variation between consecutive frames after optical-flow warping. NPES preserves the v2 jitter improvement because:

1. **Applied after temporal EMA**: NPES is inserted after the temporal EMA step, so it operates on already-stabilized alpha values. It does not interfere with the EMA's smoothing.
2. **Smooth spatial profile**: The Gaussian-complement sink potential is \(C^\infty\) smooth. Small frame-to-frame variations in the signed distance or boundary position produce proportionally small changes in the correction, rather than abrupt jumps.
3. **Background-distance stability**: The LAB background distance \(b_{\text{LAB}}\) is relatively stable across frames (it depends on the static background model, not the current frame's noise). This means the gate \(G(p)\) is temporally consistent.
4. **No iterative convergence issue**: NPES is a single-pass closed-form correction, not an iterative solver that might converge to different fixed points on different frames.

## 7. Solver / Update Strategy

NPES is a **single-pass, closed-form local correction**. No iterations or variational solve required.

### Compute steps (per frame)

```
Step 1: Compute signed distance field d(p) from alpha0 boundary.
         → cv2.distanceTransform on alpha0 > 0.5 and its complement.
         → Combine with sign: d = d_interior * (-1) + d_exterior * (+1).
         Cost: O(N) via OpenCV distance transform.

Step 2: Compute exterior projection e(p) = max(0, d(p)).
         → Single numpy clip.

Step 3: Compute sink potential S(p) = 1 - exp(-e^2 / (2 * sigma_d^2)).
         → Elementwise numpy.

Step 4: Compute background gate G(p) = (1 - b_LAB)^beta.
         → b_LAB already exists in pipeline. Elementwise numpy.

Step 5: Compute confidence gate W_C(p) = clamp((C - gamma) / (1 - gamma), 0, 1).
         → C already exists in pipeline. Elementwise numpy.

Step 6: Compute correction: delta = -lambda_s * S * G * W_C * alpha.
         → Elementwise multiply.

Step 7: Apply: alpha_corrected = clamp(alpha + delta, 0, 1).
```

Total cost: one distance transform + five elementwise operations. Fully streaming-friendly. No dependency on future frames.

## 8. Pseudocode

```python
def apply_npes(alpha, alpha0, b_lab, confidence,
               lambda_s=0.45, sigma_d=3.0, beta=2.0, gamma=0.15):
    """
    Normal-Projected Exterior Sink.
    
    Args:
        alpha:      (H, W) float32, current refined alpha in [0, 1]
        alpha0:     (H, W) float32, anchor binary mask
        b_lab:      (H, W) float32, normalized LAB background distance in [0, 1]
        confidence: (H, W) float32, CNVM confidence map in [0, 1]
        lambda_s:   sink strength
        sigma_d:    signed-distance falloff scale in pixels
        beta:       background-distance gating exponent
        gamma:      confidence floor for sink activation
    
    Returns:
        alpha_corrected: (H, W) float32, corrected alpha
    """
    # Step 1: Signed distance field
    mask_fg = (alpha0 > 0.5).astype(np.uint8)
    mask_bg = 1 - mask_fg
    
    d_ext = cv2.distanceTransform(mask_fg, cv2.DIST_L2, 5).astype(np.float32)
    # d_ext is distance from bg pixels to nearest fg pixel — BUT we want
    # distance from each pixel to the boundary.
    # Actually: distanceTransform(mask_bg) gives distance of fg pixels to boundary
    # distanceTransform(mask_fg) gives distance of bg pixels to boundary
    # We want: positive outside fg, negative inside fg
    
    d_inside = cv2.distanceTransform(mask_fg, cv2.DIST_L2, 5).astype(np.float32)
    d_outside = cv2.distanceTransform(mask_bg, cv2.DIST_L2, 5).astype(np.float32)
    
    # signed distance: positive = exterior (background side)
    signed_d = np.where(mask_fg > 0, -d_outside, d_inside)
    
    # Step 2: Exterior projection (positive part only)
    e = np.maximum(signed_d, 0.0)
    
    # Step 3: Sink potential (Gaussian complement)
    S = 1.0 - np.exp(-(e ** 2) / (2.0 * sigma_d ** 2))
    
    # Step 4: Background-distance gate
    G = np.power(np.clip(1.0 - b_lab, 0.0, 1.0), beta)
    
    # Step 5: Confidence gate
    if gamma < 1.0:
        W_C = np.clip((confidence - gamma) / (1.0 - gamma), 0.0, 1.0)
    else:
        W_C = np.ones_like(confidence)
    
    # Step 6: Compute correction
    delta = -lambda_s * S * G * W_C * alpha
    
    # Step 7: Apply
    alpha_corrected = np.clip(alpha + delta, 0.0, 1.0)
    
    return alpha_corrected
```

### Narrow-Band Optimization

For performance, restrict computation to the narrow band mask:

```python
def apply_npes_banded(alpha, alpha0, b_lab, confidence, band_mask,
                      lambda_s=0.45, sigma_d=3.0, beta=2.0, gamma=0.15):
    """Narrow-band variant — only computes within band_mask."""
    # Signed distance still computed full-frame (cheap via OpenCV)
    mask_fg = (alpha0 > 0.5).astype(np.uint8)
    mask_bg = 1 - mask_fg
    d_inside = cv2.distanceTransform(mask_fg, cv2.DIST_L2, 5).astype(np.float32)
    d_outside = cv2.distanceTransform(mask_bg, cv2.DIST_L2, 5).astype(np.float32)
    signed_d = np.where(mask_fg > 0, -d_outside, d_inside)
    
    # Only process band pixels
    bp = band_mask > 0
    e_band = np.maximum(signed_d[bp], 0.0)
    S_band = 1.0 - np.exp(-(e_band ** 2) / (2.0 * sigma_d ** 2))
    G_band = np.power(np.clip(1.0 - b_lab[bp], 0.0, 1.0), beta)
    W_band = np.clip((confidence[bp] - gamma) / max(1.0 - gamma, 1e-8), 0.0, 1.0)
    
    delta_band = -lambda_s * S_band * G_band * W_band * alpha[bp]
    
    result = alpha.copy()
    result[bp] = np.clip(alpha[bp] + delta_band, 0.0, 1.0)
    return result
```

## 9. Insertion Points in Current Pipeline

The NPES correction inserts as a single new step in the existing pipeline:

```
[existing] confidence map computation       ← provides C(p)
[existing] narrow band computation          ← provides band_mask
[existing] alpha update / refinement        ← produces refined alpha
[existing] temporal EMA over warped alpha   ← stabilizes alpha
                                            
  ──► [NEW] NPES exterior sink correction   ← INSERT HERE
                                            
[existing] edge cleanup / despill           ← final polish
[existing] optional edge decontamination
```

### Why this insertion point:

- **After temporal EMA**: NPES operates on the EMA-stabilized alpha, so it does not fight the temporal smoother. The EMA has already done its job; NPES only removes the exterior-side residual that the EMA incorrectly preserved.
- **Before edge cleanup**: Edge cleanup (morphological operations, despill) can then operate on the already-corrected alpha. This prevents edge cleanup from fighting bleed that NPES has already removed.
- **After alpha update**: The refinement step produces the soft transition zone. NPES trims only its exterior tail, leaving the interior and boundary zone intact.

### Integration with existing signals:

| Signal | Source | Used by NPES as |
|--------|--------|-----------------|
| `confidence` | CNVM confidence map | Confidence gate \(W_C\) |
| `band_mask` | Narrow band computation | Spatial restriction |
| `alpha` | After temporal EMA step | Input alpha to correct |
| `alpha0` | Anchor alpha (frame-1 based) | Signed distance source |
| `b_lab` | LAB Mahalanobis distance | Background-distance gate \(G\) |

No new signals need to be computed. All inputs already exist in the pipeline.

## 10. Five-Pass Ablation Plan

Each pass enables one more component of NPES. This isolates the effect of each term.

| Pass | Name | \(\lambda_s\) | \(\sigma_d\) | \(\beta\) | \(\gamma\) | Description |
|------|------|-------------|-------------|---------|---------|-------------|
| P1 | `npes_sink_only` | 0.35 | 3.0 | 0.0 | 0.0 | Sink potential only. \(\beta=0 \Rightarrow G=1\), \(\gamma=0 \Rightarrow W_C=1\). Pure exterior signed-distance clamping. Measures raw anti-bleed effect and any foreground thinning. |
| P2 | `npes_bg_gated` | 0.35 | 3.0 | 2.0 | 0.0 | Add background-distance gate. \(G = (1-b_{\text{LAB}})^2\). Should recover foreground detail at exterior positions where color differs from background. |
| P3 | `npes_conf_gated` | 0.35 | 3.0 | 2.0 | 0.15 | Add confidence gate. Should preserve anti-chatter in ambiguous zones. |
| P4 | `npes_tuned_moderate` | 0.45 | 2.5 | 2.0 | 0.15 | Increase sink strength and tighten falloff. More aggressive bleed removal. Check for thinning. |
| P5 | `npes_tuned_aggressive` | 0.55 | 2.0 | 1.5 | 0.10 | Push parameters harder. Lower \(\beta\) = less foreground protection. Lower \(\gamma\) = sink fires in more ambiguous zones. This is the "how far can we go" test. |

### Expected outcomes:

- **P1**: Strong bleed reduction, possible foreground thinning at hair/detail, possible chatter increase (no confidence gate).
- **P2**: Similar bleed reduction, less thinning (background gate protects foreground-colored pixels).
- **P3**: Similar bleed + thinning as P2, but chatter should return to v2-level low (confidence gate active).
- **P4**: Better bleed than P3 due to stronger \(\lambda_s\) and tighter \(\sigma_d\). This is the expected sweet spot.
- **P5**: Maximum bleed reduction. If thinning or chatter regress, this tells us the parameter limits.

### Concrete metric targets:

| Metric | P3 target | P4 target | P5 limit |
|--------|-----------|-----------|----------|
| border_bleed | ≤ 0.0070 | ≤ 0.0065 | ≤ 0.0060 |
| chatter | ≤ 0.0035 | ≤ 0.0035 | ≤ 0.0050 |
| temporal_jitter | ≤ 0.0270 | ≤ 0.0270 | ≤ 0.0280 |
| mean_alpha | ≥ 0.435 | ≥ 0.430 | ≥ 0.425 |

## 11. Automatic Failure Metrics

### Exterior Bleed Detection

Already measured as `border_bleed` in the existing harness. Additionally, define a **directional bleed metric** for more granular diagnosis:

```python
def measure_exterior_bleed(alpha, alpha0, threshold=0.01):
    """Fraction of exterior-side narrow-band pixels with alpha > threshold."""
    mask_fg = (alpha0 > 0.5).astype(np.uint8)
    d_ext = cv2.distanceTransform(mask_fg, cv2.DIST_L2, 5)
    exterior_band = (d_ext > 0) & (d_ext < 8)  # exterior within 8px
    if exterior_band.sum() == 0:
        return 0.0
    return float((alpha[exterior_band] > threshold).mean())
```

### Foreground Thinning Detection

Compare mean alpha in the **interior** narrow band between the NPES result and the v2 baseline:

```python
def measure_fg_thinning(alpha_npes, alpha_v2, alpha0, max_acceptable_loss=0.02):
    """Mean alpha loss on interior side. Flag if > max_acceptable_loss."""
    mask_fg = (alpha0 > 0.5).astype(np.uint8)
    mask_bg = 1 - mask_fg
    d_int = cv2.distanceTransform(mask_bg, cv2.DIST_L2, 5)
    interior_band = (d_int > 0) & (d_int < 6)
    if interior_band.sum() == 0:
        return 0.0
    loss = float((alpha_v2[interior_band] - alpha_npes[interior_band]).mean())
    return loss  # positive = thinning; flag if > max_acceptable_loss
```

### Temporal Ghosting Detection

Measure alpha residual in the far exterior (beyond the narrow band) where alpha should be exactly zero:

```python
def measure_temporal_ghosting(alpha, alpha0, far_threshold=12):
    """Mean alpha beyond far_threshold pixels from boundary."""
    mask_fg = (alpha0 > 0.5).astype(np.uint8)
    d_ext = cv2.distanceTransform(mask_fg, cv2.DIST_L2, 5)
    far_exterior = d_ext > far_threshold
    if far_exterior.sum() == 0:
        return 0.0
    return float(alpha[far_exterior].mean())
```

### Chatter Relapse Detection

Use the existing `chatter` metric. Additionally, compute a **per-region chatter** restricted to the exterior band to detect if the sink introduces new instability:

```python
def measure_exterior_chatter(alpha_seq, alpha0_seq, band_width=6):
    """Frame-to-frame alpha variance in the exterior narrow band."""
    diffs = []
    for t in range(1, len(alpha_seq)):
        mask_fg = (alpha0_seq[t] > 0.5).astype(np.uint8)
        d_ext = cv2.distanceTransform(mask_fg, cv2.DIST_L2, 5)
        ext_band = (d_ext > 0) & (d_ext < band_width)
        if ext_band.sum() == 0:
            continue
        diff = np.abs(alpha_seq[t][ext_band] - alpha_seq[t-1][ext_band])
        diffs.append(diff.mean())
    return float(np.mean(diffs)) if diffs else 0.0
```

### Automatic pass/fail gates:

| Metric | PASS | WARN | FAIL |
|--------|------|------|------|
| border_bleed | ≤ 0.0065 | 0.0065–0.0075 | > 0.0075 |
| fg_thinning | ≤ 0.010 | 0.010–0.020 | > 0.020 |
| chatter | ≤ 0.0035 | 0.0035–0.0050 | > 0.0050 |
| temporal_jitter | ≤ 0.0270 | 0.0270–0.0285 | > 0.0285 |
| temporal_ghosting | ≤ 0.001 | 0.001–0.005 | > 0.005 |
| mean_alpha | ≥ 0.430 | 0.425–0.430 | < 0.425 |

## 12. Patch Sketch

### `alpha_fix/config.py` additions

```python
# --- NPES: Normal-Projected Exterior Sink ---
NPES_ENABLED: bool = True
NPES_LAMBDA_S: float = 0.45       # Sink strength [0.0 - 1.0]
NPES_SIGMA_D: float = 2.5         # Signed-distance falloff scale (pixels)
NPES_BETA: float = 2.0            # Background-distance gating exponent
NPES_GAMMA: float = 0.15          # Confidence floor for sink activation
NPES_BAND_ONLY: bool = True       # Restrict to narrow band for performance
```

### `alpha_fix/pipeline.py` additions

```python
# ---------- NPES helper ----------

def _compute_signed_distance(alpha0: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:
    """Signed distance field from alpha0 boundary. Positive = exterior."""
    mask_fg = (alpha0 > 0.5).astype(np.uint8)
    mask_bg = (1 - mask_fg).astype(np.uint8)
    # Distance of interior pixels to boundary
    d_interior = cv2.distanceTransform(mask_bg, cv2.DIST_L2, 5).astype(np.float32)
    # Distance of exterior pixels to boundary
    d_exterior = cv2.distanceTransform(mask_fg, cv2.DIST_L2, 5).astype(np.float32)
    # Combine: negative inside, positive outside
    signed_d = np.where(mask_fg > 0, -d_interior, d_exterior)
    return signed_d


def apply_npes(
    alpha: np.ndarray,
    alpha0: np.ndarray,
    b_lab: np.ndarray,
    confidence: np.ndarray,
    band_mask: np.ndarray | None = None,
    lambda_s: float = 0.45,
    sigma_d: float = 2.5,
    beta: float = 2.0,
    gamma: float = 0.15,
) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Normal-Projected Exterior Sink.
    Reduces alpha on the exterior (background) side of the boundary
    without affecting the interior (foreground) side.
    """
    signed_d = _compute_signed_distance(alpha0)

    # Exterior projection
    e = np.maximum(signed_d, 0.0)

    # Sink potential: Gaussian complement
    S = 1.0 - np.exp(-(e ** 2) / (2.0 * sigma_d ** 2))

    # Background-distance gate
    G = np.power(np.clip(1.0 - b_lab, 0.0, 1.0), beta)

    # Confidence gate
    denom = max(1.0 - gamma, 1e-8)
    W_C = np.clip((confidence - gamma) / denom, 0.0, 1.0)

    # Correction (always non-positive)
    delta = -lambda_s * S * G * W_C * alpha

    # Apply with optional band restriction
    if band_mask is not None:
        result = alpha.copy()
        bp = band_mask > 0
        result[bp] = np.clip(alpha[bp] + delta[bp], 0.0, 1.0)
        return result
    else:
        return np.clip(alpha + delta, 0.0, 1.0)
```

### Insertion in the main processing loop

```python
# In the per-frame processing function, after temporal EMA:

    # ... existing code ...
    alpha = apply_temporal_ema(alpha, alpha_prev_warped, ...)
    
    # ──► NEW: NPES exterior sink correction
    if config.NPES_ENABLED:
        alpha = apply_npes(
            alpha=alpha,
            alpha0=alpha0,
            b_lab=b_lab_normalized,
            confidence=confidence_map,
            band_mask=band_mask if config.NPES_BAND_ONLY else None,
            lambda_s=config.NPES_LAMBDA_S,
            sigma_d=config.NPES_SIGMA_D,
            beta=config.NPES_BETA,
            gamma=config.NPES_GAMMA,
        )
    
    # ... existing edge cleanup / despill ...
    alpha = apply_edge_cleanup(alpha, ...)
```

### Run script for the five-pass ablation
