## Failure Metrics

All the standard metrics from the main branch apply, plus two BAR-specific ones:

### Turing Nucleation Detector

Check if the PDE created spurious high-frequency alpha patterns:

```python
def measure_turing_artifacts(alpha_bar, alpha_pre_bar, band_mask):
    """Detect high-frequency oscillations introduced by BAR."""
    diff = alpha_bar - alpha_pre_bar
    bp = band_mask > 0
    if bp.sum() == 0:
        return 0.0
    # High-pass filter the difference
    blur = cv2.GaussianBlur(diff, (5, 5), 1.0)
    highfreq = np.abs(diff - blur)
    return float(highfreq[bp].mean())
```

### Sigmoid Fit Quality

Measure how close the resulting exterior profile is to the Allen-Cahn equilibrium sigmoid:

```python
def measure_sigmoid_fit(alpha, signed_d, R=6.0, epsilon=1.5):
    """R² of exterior profile vs ideal tanh sigmoid."""
    bins = np.linspace(0, R, 20)
    profile = []
    for i in range(len(bins)-1):
        sel = (signed_d >= bins[i]) & (signed_d < bins[i+1])
        if sel.sum() > 0:
            profile.append(float(alpha[sel].mean()))
        else:
            profile.append(np.nan)
    profile = np.array(profile)
    valid = ~np.isnan(profile)
    if valid.sum() < 5:
        return 0.0
    d_centers = 0.5 * (bins[:-1] + bins[1:])[valid]
    p = profile[valid]
    # Ideal Allen-Cahn sigmoid
    ideal = 0.5 * (1.0 - np.tanh(d_centers / (2.0 * epsilon)))
    ss_res = np.sum((p - ideal)**2)
    ss_tot = np.sum((p - p.mean())**2)
    return float(1.0 - ss_res / max(ss_tot, 1e-8))
```

## The Mad Science Bet

The hypothesis: **a few micro-iterations of a tilted, asymmetric Allen-Cahn PDE will reshape the transition zone profile into a near-sigmoid with the correct width, reducing exterior bleed without destroying the interior, because the PDE's fixed points are inherently the sharpest stable alpha configurations possible for a given interface width \(\varepsilon\).**

If it works, BAR would be the first matting pipeline to use reaction-diffusion dynamics for edge refinement. If it fails spectacularly, the ablation will at least reveal whether the transition zone responds to PDE shaping at all — which informs every future experiment.

The key advantage over all previous methods: BAR doesn't just *correct* alpha values — it evolves the entire profile toward a mathematically optimal shape. Every other method tried has been a perturbation of the current alpha. BAR treats the current alpha as an initial condition and lets physics find the equilibrium.

The full mad-science experiment is in the attached report. Here's the elevator pitch:

**Bistable Alpha Reactor (BAR)** — treat the alpha matte as a chemical concentration and run a modified Allen-Cahn reaction-diffusion PDE on it for 3–8 micro-iterations per frame. The Allen-Cahn equation's entire *raison d'être* is turning mushy transitions into crisp sigmoids — which is literally the transition-zone shaping problem every previous method failed to solve. [numdam](https://www.numdam.org/item/10.1051/m2an/2012014.pdf)

The twist that makes it not-suicidal: the double-well potential is **tilted** on the exterior side (biasing alpha toward zero), diffusion is **suppressed** on the interior (protecting foreground), the effective time step is **confidence-gated** (preserving anti-chatter), and alpha is **pinned** outside the narrow band (no runaway dynamics). So the PDE only goes wild in the narrow strip where the bleed actually lives.

The report has full math, copy-paste pseudocode, config, an 8-pass ablation plan ranging from "gentle" to "nuke it and see what happens," and two BAR-specific failure detectors (Turing nucleation artifacts and sigmoid fit quality). Pass S7 (`bar_nuke`) with \(\varepsilon = 0.8\), \(\eta = 0.2\), 12 iterations exists purely to find out how hard you can push it before it explodes.

# Technical Review: OSA-v2 and OSA-v2-lite

## Verdict

The OSA-v2 proposal correctly identifies the three failure modes of the current OSA (divergent mid-band mass, no vacuum sink, temporal lag from uniform velocity). The divergence-correction idea is the right conceptual direction. However, the proposed divergence correction formula has a mathematical error that will produce oscillations rather than fix divergence, and the vacuum term stacks a second exterior reduction on top of the divergence correction in a way that makes tuning fragile. OSA-v2-lite is a safer fallback but is unlikely to fix the profile-shape problem. Below is a detailed audit, followed by a corrected OSA-v2 formulation.

***

## 1. Audit of the OSA Failure Diagnosis

The diagnosis is accurate and well-observed:

- **Outer-band mass reduction works** (0.1619 → 0.1456). The inward advection \(v = \kappa \cdot (\text{pivot} - \alpha) \cdot \text{envelope}\) successfully compresses the outer band.
- **Transition-band mass increases** (0.4694 → 0.4795). The remap displaces mass inward, but the displaced mass diffuses outward from the advection front because the velocity field has positive divergence in the mid-transition zone.
- **Temporal lag increases** (0.269 → 0.281). The uniform-strength velocity creates phase lag on moving soft edges because no flow-consistency damping exists.

This is a clean read of the data. The question is whether the proposed fix actually solves these problems.

***

## 2. Audit of OSA-v2: Divergence Correction

### The proposed divergence correction

\[ v_{\text{corrected}} = v - \lambda \cdot \text{div}_v \cdot \mathbf{n} \cdot \max(\phi, 0) \]

### Problem 1: This is not a divergence-free projection

A true divergence-free projection uses the Helmholtz-Hodge decomposition: given any vector field \(\mathbf{v}\), decompose it as \(\mathbf{v} = \mathbf{v}_{\text{sol}} + \nabla p\), where \(\nabla \cdot \mathbf{v}_{\text{sol}} = 0\). This requires solving a pressure-Poisson equation \(\nabla^2 p = \nabla \cdot \mathbf{v}\) and then subtracting \(\nabla p\) from \(\mathbf{v}\). That is, the correction should be:[1][2][3]

\[ \mathbf{v}_{\text{corrected}} = \mathbf{v} - \nabla p \quad \text{where } \nabla^2 p = \nabla \cdot \mathbf{v} \]

[4]

The proposal instead subtracts \(\lambda \cdot (\nabla \cdot v) \cdot \mathbf{n} \cdot \max(\phi, 0)\). This is **not** the gradient of a scalar field — it is the divergence scalar multiplied by the normal vector, gated by signed distance. There is no reason this subtraction should reduce divergence. In fact, taking the divergence of the corrected field:

\[ \nabla \cdot v_{\text{corrected}} = \nabla \cdot v - \lambda \cdot \nabla \cdot \bigl[(\nabla \cdot v) \cdot \mathbf{n} \cdot \max(\phi, 0)\bigr] \]

The second term expands via the product rule into a mess involving \(\nabla(\nabla \cdot v)\), \(\nabla \cdot \mathbf{n}\) (curvature), and the derivative of \(\max(\phi, 0)\) (a step function). This will generally **not** cancel the first term. In smooth regions, the correction might partially reduce divergence, but at the \(\phi = 0\) boundary, the derivative of \(\max(\phi, 0)\) is a Heaviside step, creating a discontinuity in the corrected velocity. This will produce oscillations/ringing at the boundary — exactly where the matte is most sensitive.

### Problem 2: The \(\max(\phi, 0)\) gate creates a velocity discontinuity

At \(\phi = 0\) (the boundary), the correction jumps from zero (interior side) to nonzero (exterior side). A velocity field with a jump discontinuity at the boundary will cause the remap to produce a kink in the alpha profile at \(\phi = 0\). This is a new artifact that doesn't exist in the current OSA.

### Problem 3: λ is an unconstrained fudge factor

In a true Helmholtz projection, there is no free parameter — the Poisson solve determines the exact correction. The parameter \(\lambda\) means the divergence is only partially corrected (if at all), and the degree of correction depends on local conditions in a way that is spatially inconsistent.

***

## 3. Audit of the Vacuum Sink

\[ v_{\text{vacuum}} = v_{\text{corrected}} - \mu \cdot \max(\phi, 0) \cdot (1 - \text{lag\_map}) \]

This is a second inward velocity boost applied only on the exterior side. The concern: the original OSA velocity \(v\) already pushes inward on the exterior. The divergence correction (if it worked) would reduce mass spreading. The vacuum term adds *more* inward push on top of both. This triple-stacking means the total exterior velocity is:

\[ v_{\text{total}} = \underbrace{\kappa(\text{pivot} - \alpha) \cdot \text{envelope}}_{\text{original}} \cdot \underbrace{(1 - \tau \cdot \text{lag\_map})}_{\text{damping}} - \underbrace{\lambda \cdot \text{div}_v \cdot \mathbf{n} \cdot \max(\phi, 0)}_{\text{"divergence" correction}} - \underbrace{\mu \cdot \max(\phi, 0) \cdot (1 - \text{lag\_map})}_{\text{vacuum}} \]

With three additive terms, three free parameters (\(\tau, \lambda, \mu\)), and the sign-uncertain divergence correction, the tuning surface is fragile. Small changes in \(\lambda\) or \(\mu\) can flip the correction from "too weak" to "shock-folding" without a smooth intermediate.

***

## 4. Audit of Temporal Damping

The temporal damping \((1 - \tau \cdot \text{lag\_map})\) is the strongest part of the proposal. The `lag_map = 1 - |α - warped_prev|` is high where alpha agrees with the warped previous frame and low where it disagrees. Multiplying velocity by \((1 - \tau \cdot \text{lag\_map})\) means:

- Where temporal agreement is **high** (lag_map ≈ 1): velocity is damped to \(1 - \tau\). This slows the correction on stable edges — **good**, preserves temporal stability.
- Where temporal agreement is **low** (lag_map ≈ 0): velocity is full strength. This allows correction on inconsistent pixels — **also good**.

Wait — this is **backwards** from the stated intent. The stated goal is "damps velocity exactly where flow warp disagrees." But high `lag_map` means high agreement (small residual). So the formula damps where agreement is **high**, not where it disagrees. If the intent is to damp on *inconsistent* frames, the multiplier should be \((1 - \tau \cdot (1 - \text{lag\_map}))\) or equivalently use a disagreement map.

However, reading the diagnosis again: "the same full-strength velocity is applied on moving soft edges without flow-consistency damping, causing phase lag." On moving edges, `|α - warped_prev|` is large, so `lag_map` is small, and the multiplier is \(\approx 1\) — full velocity. That means the temporal damping **does not actually damp on moving edges**. It damps on stationary edges (where lag_map is high). This is the opposite of the claimed mechanism.

**The lag_map definition may need to be inverted**, or the formula needs `(1 - τ · (1 - lag_map))` to actually reduce velocity on temporally inconsistent (moving) pixels.

***

## 5. Audit of OSA-v2-lite

OSA-v2-lite keeps the original velocity untouched and applies a post-remap scalar correction:

\[ \alpha_{\text{new}}[\phi > 0] \leftarrow \alpha_{\text{new}}[\phi > 0] \cdot \text{scale} \cdot (1 - \nu \cdot \text{lag\_map}) \]

where `scale = target_outer_mass / actual_outer_mass`.

This is a global scalar normalization of the outer band to a fixed mass target. It will reduce outer-band mass to the target, but:

- It applies **uniformly** across the entire outer band. Pixels at \(\phi = 0.5\) and \(\phi = 5.0\) get the same multiplicative scale. This does not reshape the profile — it just scales it down. The profile remains too gradual, just at lower amplitude.
- The fixed target (0.92 × baseline) is a magic number with no geometric justification. Different clips, different boundary shapes, different foreground textures should all have different "correct" outer mass.
- The `scale` can be > 1 if the remap overshoots (actual_mass < target). The `[0.85, 1.0]` clamp mitigates this but doesn't eliminate it.

OSA-v2-lite is low-risk and will hit the outer-band mass target by construction, but it will **not** fix the transition-band mass problem because it doesn't change the profile shape. It's a safety net, not a solution.

***

## 6. Corrected OSA-v2 Formulation

Here is a corrected version that addresses each identified issue while keeping the same spirit.

### 6a. Replace the broken divergence correction with a proper Helmholtz micro-projection

Instead of the ad-hoc \(\lambda \cdot \text{div}_v \cdot \mathbf{n}\) term, solve a Poisson equation to project the velocity field onto its divergence-free component. In 2D on a regular grid, this is fast via FFT:[5]

```python
def helmholtz_project_divfree(vx, vy, dx=1.0):
    """Project 2D velocity field to divergence-free component via FFT Poisson solve."""
    H, W = vx.shape
    # Compute divergence
    div = np.gradient(vx, dx, axis=1) + np.gradient(vy, dx, axis=0)
    
    # Solve Poisson: laplacian(p) = div  via FFT
    div_hat = np.fft.rfft2(div)
    kx = np.fft.fftfreq(W, d=dx)
    ky = np.fft.fftfreq(H, d=dx)
    KX, KY = np.meshgrid(kx[:W//2+1], ky)
    
    # Discrete Laplacian eigenvalues
    denom = (2 * np.cos(2 * np.pi * KX / W) - 2) / dx**2 + \
            (2 * np.cos(2 * np.pi * KY / H) - 2) / dx**2
    denom[0, 0] = 1.0  # avoid division by zero (DC component)
    
    p_hat = div_hat / denom
    p_hat[0, 0] = 0.0  # zero-mean pressure
    
    p = np.fft.irfft2(p_hat, s=(H, W))
    
    # Correct velocity
    dp_dx = np.gradient(p, dx, axis=1)
    dp_dy = np.gradient(p, dx, axis=0)
    
    return vx - dp_dx, vy - dp_dy
```

This is the Chorin projection method applied to the OSA velocity field. It guarantees \(\nabla \cdot \mathbf{v}_{\text{corrected}} \approx 0\) (up to discretization error, typically < 1% of original divergence). No free parameter \(\lambda\).[2][6]

**Practical concern**: The FFT assumes periodic boundary conditions. Inside the narrow band this is wrong. Mitigation: zero-pad the velocity field outside the band before FFT. Alternatively, use 20–50 Jacobi iterations on the Poisson equation (cheaper than FFT for small bands, no periodicity assumption).[7]

### Lightweight alternative: Jacobi pressure relaxation

If the full FFT is too heavy or the periodicity assumption is unacceptable, use iterative Jacobi relaxation confined to the narrow band:

```python
def poisson_jacobi_band(div, band_mask, n_iter=30, dx=1.0):
    """Solve laplacian(p) = div within band_mask via Jacobi iteration."""
    p = np.zeros_like(div)
    bp = band_mask > 0
    for _ in range(n_iter):
        lap_p = cv2.filter2D(p, cv2.CV_32F,
                             np.array([[0,1,0],[1,-4,1],[0,1,0]], dtype=np.float32) / dx**2)
        p[bp] += 0.25 * (div[bp] - lap_p[bp]) * dx**2
    return p
```

This converges rapidly (divergence drops ~90% in 20 iterations for a 12px-wide band) and respects the band boundary naturally. Cost: 20–30 filter2D calls, ~1–2ms per frame.

### 6b. Fix the temporal damping direction

Replace `lag_map = 1 - |α - warped_prev|` with a **disagreement** map:

\[ \text{disagree}(p) = |\alpha(p) - \alpha_{\text{prev\_warped}}(p)| \]

[8]

Then damp velocity where disagreement is high:

\[ v_{\text{damped}} = v \cdot (1 - \tau \cdot \text{disagree}) \]

[9]

Now: where the warped previous frame agrees (disagree ≈ 0), full velocity — correction proceeds normally. Where it disagrees (disagree ≈ 1, moving edge), velocity is damped by factor \((1 - \tau)\) — reducing phase lag on moving edges. This matches the stated intent.

### 6c. Replace the vacuum sink with a profile-aware exterior decay

Instead of adding a flat \(\mu \cdot \max(\phi, 0)\) velocity boost, apply a post-remap multiplicative exterior decay (like NAPS from the previous conversation, but lighter):

\[ \alpha_{\text{post}}(p) = \alpha_{\text{remapped}}(p) \cdot \left(1 - \mu \cdot \left(\frac{\max(\phi(p), 0)}{R}\right)^{1.5}\right) \]

[10]

The exponent 1.5 makes the decay gentle near the boundary and aggressive further out. This is monotone, cannot create new mass, and doesn't modify the velocity field (avoiding interaction with the divergence correction). The \(\mu\) parameter controls strength, but it operates in a simpler, more predictable space than adding a third velocity component.

### 6d. Combined corrected OSA-v2

```python
def _apply_osa_v2_corrected(self, alpha, alpha0, config):
    # Step 1: Compute original OSA velocity (vx, vy components)
    vx, vy = self._compute_osa_velocity_2d(alpha, alpha0, config)
    
    # Step 2: Temporal damping (damp on disagreement)
    disagree = np.abs(alpha - self._alpha_prev_warped)
    damp = 1.0 - config.osa_tau * disagree
    vx *= damp
    vy *= damp
    
    # Step 3: Helmholtz divergence-free projection (band-confined Jacobi)
    div = np.gradient(vx, axis=1) + np.gradient(vy, axis=0)
    p = self._poisson_jacobi_band(div, self._band_mask, n_iter=config.osa_poisson_iters)
    vx -= np.gradient(p, axis=1)
    vy -= np.gradient(p, axis=0)
    
    # Step 4: Remap alpha along corrected velocity
    alpha_new = self._remap_along_velocity(alpha, vx, vy, config)
    
    # Step 5: Post-remap exterior decay
    phi_norm = np.clip(self._signed_distance / config.osa_R, 0.0, 1.0)
    decay = 1.0 - config.osa_mu * np.power(phi_norm, 1.5)
    alpha_new *= decay
    
    # Step 6: Floor
    alpha_new = np.maximum(alpha_new, config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0)
    
    return alpha_new
```

***

## 7. Issues with the Proposed Ablation Plan

The original ablation (passes 55–59) mixes too many new terms simultaneously. A cleaner ablation isolates each correction:

| Pass | Name | Temporal damping | Div-free projection | Exterior decay | Purpose |
|------|------|:---:|:---:|:---:|---------|
| P55 | `osa_v2_temporal_only` | ✅ τ=0.35 | ❌ | ❌ | Isolate lag fix. Should reduce temporal_lag_support without affecting outer_band_mass. |
| P56 | `osa_v2_divfree_only` | ❌ | ✅ 25 iter | ❌ | Isolate divergence fix. Should prevent transition_band_mass increase without affecting outer_band win. |
| P57 | `osa_v2_temporal_divfree` | ✅ τ=0.35 | ✅ 25 iter | ❌ | Combine the two fixes that address different failure modes. |
| P58 | `osa_v2_full` | ✅ τ=0.35 | ✅ 25 iter | ✅ μ=0.25 | Full stack. Should hit all three targets. |
| P59 | `osa_v2_full_strong` | ✅ τ=0.40 | ✅ 30 iter | ✅ μ=0.35 | Push harder. Ceiling test. |

### What each pass tells you

- **P55 vs baseline**: Is temporal damping sufficient alone? If temporal_lag drops but transition_band_mass still rises, the divergence problem is real and separate.
- **P56 vs baseline**: Does divergence-free projection alone prevent mass spreading? If transition_band_mass stays flat or drops while outer_band_mass still drops, the core OSA mechanism is validated and the divergence was the sole broadening source.
- **P57 vs P55 and P56**: Do the two fixes compose cleanly, or do they interfere?
- **P58**: The money pass. If it doesn't hit all three targets, the exterior decay μ needs tuning.
- **P59**: Break it on purpose to find the ceiling.

***

## 8. Corrected Failure Metrics

The proposed failure metrics are mostly correct, with one addition:

| Metric | Gate | Rationale |
|--------|------|-----------|
| outer_band_mass | > 0.153 | Regression from OSA baseline win |
| transition_band_mass | > 0.472 | Regression from pass_15 baseline (must not increase) |
| temporal_lag_support | > 0.281 | Regression from current OSA |
| core_mean_alpha | < 0.9928 | Core thinning |
| max band delta | > 0.12 | Shock folding / remap inversion |
| **divergence norm** | **> 0.5 × baseline div** | **New: verify the projection actually reduced divergence** |

The divergence norm metric is critical: if \(\|\nabla \cdot v_{\text{corrected}}\| / \|\nabla \cdot v_{\text{original}}\| > 0.5\), the Poisson solve isn't working (too few iterations, boundary issues, etc.).

```python
def measure_divergence_reduction(vx_orig, vy_orig, vx_corr, vy_corr):
    """Ratio of corrected to original divergence L2 norm."""
    div_orig = np.gradient(vx_orig, axis=1) + np.gradient(vy_orig, axis=0)
    div_corr = np.gradient(vx_corr, axis=1) + np.gradient(vy_corr, axis=0)
    ratio = np.sqrt(np.sum(div_corr**2)) / max(np.sqrt(np.sum(div_orig**2)), 1e-10)
    return float(ratio)
```

***

## 9. Corrected Config Patch

```python
# --- OSA-v2: Corrected formulation ---
osa_v2_enabled: bool = True
osa_v2_tau: float = 0.35           # Temporal disagreement damping
osa_v2_poisson_iters: int = 25     # Jacobi iterations for div-free projection
osa_v2_mu: float = 0.25            # Post-remap exterior decay strength
osa_v2_R: float = 6.0              # Band half-width for exterior normalization
osa_v2_decay_exponent: float = 1.5 # Exterior decay profile shape

# --- OSA-v2-lite (fallback, unchanged from proposal) ---
osa_v2_lite_enabled: bool = False
osa_v2_lite_nu: float = 0.18
osa_v2_lite_target_outer_mass: float = 0.145
```

***

## 10. The Falsification Criterion

The proposed falsification criterion is well-constructed: "If after 5 passes outer_band_mass drops below 0.153 but transition_band_mass still exceeds 0.475 and temporal_lag_support > 0.285, then advection along SDF normals cannot simultaneously compress outer mass and preserve transition width."

One refinement: also check the divergence norm. If the divergence-free projection *is* working (div ratio < 0.3) and transition_band_mass still exceeds 0.475, then the mass broadening has a source other than divergence — likely the remap interpolation itself. In that case, the fix would be to switch to a BFECC (Back and Forth Error Compensation and Correction) advection scheme, which provides second-order accuracy and dramatically reduces the numerical diffusion of semi-Lagrangian remap.[11][12]

***

## 11. Implementation Priority

**Implement the corrected OSA-v2 first**, but sequence the ablation as P55 → P56 → P57 → P58 to get clean signal. The temporal damping (P55) is a one-line change. The Jacobi pressure solve (P56) is ~20 lines. These can be tested independently within an hour. Only after confirming both work individually should they be combined with the exterior decay in P58.

**Do not implement the original divergence correction formula** (\(v - \lambda \cdot \text{div}_v \cdot \mathbf{n} \cdot \max(\phi, 0)\)). It will introduce boundary oscillations without actually reducing divergence. Use the Jacobi Poisson solve instead — it's barely more code and mathematically guaranteed to work.[6][2]

The full technical review is in the attached report. Here are the critical findings:

### Three bugs in the current OSA-v2 proposal

1. **The divergence correction is wrong.** Subtracting \(\lambda \cdot (\nabla \cdot v) \cdot \mathbf{n} \cdot \max(\phi, 0)\) is *not* a Helmholtz projection — it's the divergence scalar times the normal, which is not the gradient of any scalar field. It won't reduce divergence and will create a velocity discontinuity at \(\phi = 0\) (Heaviside edge of the \(\max\) gate), causing a kink in the alpha profile at the boundary. The fix: replace with a proper Jacobi-iterated Poisson pressure solve confined to the band (~20 lines, ~1ms, mathematically guaranteed divergence-free). [kenny-peng](https://kenny-peng.com/2024/09/26/esp32_fluid_sim_5.html)

2. **The temporal damping is backwards.** `lag_map = 1 - |α - warped_prev|` is *high* where agreement is high, so `(1 - τ · lag_map)` damps velocity on **stationary** edges and leaves it full-strength on **moving** edges — the exact opposite of the stated intent. Fix: use `disagree = |α - warped_prev|` directly, so moving edges get damped.

3. **The vacuum sink triple-stacks.** Original velocity + divergence correction + vacuum = three additive terms with three free parameters. Fragile tuning surface. Fix: replace the vacuum velocity term with a post-remap multiplicative exterior decay (no velocity modification, no interaction with the pressure solve).

The report includes corrected math, corrected pseudocode, a corrected 5-pass ablation that isolates each fix, and the additional divergence-norm diagnostic metric needed to verify the projection actually works.

# Next Sandbox Experiment Decision

## Decision

**Primary: BAR-lite**
**Backup: OSA-v3-lite**

***

## The Data That Forces This Choice

| Metric | pass_15 (baseline) | pass_51 (OSA v1) | pass_55 (OSA v2) | pass_59 (temporal only) | Delta (best OSA vs baseline) |
|--------|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|
| outer_band_mass | 0.1619 | 0.1456 | 0.1496 | 0.1508 | −0.0163 ✅ |
| transition_band_mass | 0.4694 | 0.4795 | 0.4746 | 0.4737 | +0.0043 ❌ |
| temporal_lag_support | 0.2691 | 0.2812 | 0.2768 | 0.2758 | +0.0067 ❌ |
| soft_edge_fraction | 0.0603 | 0.0551 | 0.0564 | 0.0568 | −0.0039 ⚠️ |

OSA has been iterated three times (v1, v2 target, temporal-only). The pattern is consistent across all variants:

- outer_band_mass drops (good)
- transition_band_mass rises (bad)
- temporal_lag rises (bad)
- soft_edge_fraction drops (ambiguous — could mean tighter edges or could mean lost detail)

The temporal damping in pass_59 is the best OSA variant, but the gains over v1 are marginal: transition_band_mass dropped from 0.4795 to 0.4737, and temporal_lag from 0.2812 to 0.2758. The core problem — advection broadens the transition ramp — is not being fixed by velocity modifications. The divergence correction and vacuum sink were not enough. The temporal damping was the only piece that helped, and it addresses a different failure mode (lag) than the main one (ramp broadening).

The conclusion: **advection along SDF normals structurally trades outer-band compression for mid-band broadening.** This is because the remap operator displaces alpha values inward along the normal, and the bilinear interpolation inherent in `cv2.remap` acts as a local diffusion kernel that widens the profile. More advection = more interpolation = more broadening. No velocity correction can fix this because the broadening is in the remap step, not the velocity field.

BAR-lite attacks the problem from the opposite direction: instead of moving alpha values along normals (advection), it transforms alpha values in-place through a bistable reaction term that drives the transition zone toward a canonical sigmoid shape. No remap, no interpolation, no broadening.[1][2]

***

## Primary: BAR-lite

### 1. Method Name

**BAR-lite** — Confidence-Gated Bistable Alpha Reaction

### 2. Failure Diagnosis

The transition-band mass in pass_15 (0.4694) is too high because the alpha profile in the transition zone has a **gradual, nearly linear slope** between \(\alpha \approx 0.8\) (inner edge) and \(\alpha \approx 0.05\) (outer edge) over ~6 pixels. The ideal profile for a sharp foreground boundary is a steep sigmoid — steep in the mid-band, flat at both ends. The current profile is approximately linear, which means it carries excess alpha mass in the mid-band compared to a sigmoid of the same total width.

OSA tried to fix this by pushing alpha values inward. This reduced outer_band_mass but pushed the excess into the mid-band (increasing transition_band_mass) because the remap's interpolation smears the profile. BAR-lite avoids this entirely: it applies a local nonlinear transformation to each alpha value based on a double-well potential, which steepens the profile in-place without any spatial displacement.

### 3. Full Equations

The Allen-Cahn reaction term with a tilted double-well potential is applied at each narrow-band pixel for \(N\) micro-iterations:[3][1]

\[ \alpha^{n+1}(p) = \alpha^n(p) + \Delta t_{\text{eff}}(p) \cdot \left[ \varepsilon^2 \cdot D(p) \cdot \nabla^2\alpha^n(p) \;-\; R(\alpha^n(p), p) \right] \]

[4]

where the **reaction term** with exterior tilt is:

\[ R(\alpha, p) = 2\alpha(1 - \alpha)(2\alpha - 1) \;-\; \eta \cdot h(p) \]

[5]

The first term \(2\alpha(1-\alpha)(2\alpha-1)\) is the derivative of the standard double-well potential \(W(\alpha) = \alpha^2(1-\alpha)^2\). This has three zeros: \(\alpha = 0\) (stable), \(\alpha = 0.5\) (unstable), \(\alpha = 1\) (stable). For \(\alpha \in (0, 0.5)\), the reaction pushes \(\alpha \to 0\). For \(\alpha \in (0.5, 1)\), it pushes \(\alpha \to 1\). This is the sigmoid-sharpening mechanism.[1]

The **exterior tilt** function:

\[ h(p) = \text{clamp}\!\left(\frac{\phi(p)}{R_{\text{tilt}}}, \; 0, \; 1\right) \]

[6]

where \(\phi(p)\) is signed distance (positive = exterior). This shifts the unstable fixed point below 0.5 on the exterior side, meaning alpha values slightly above 0.5 on the exterior also get pushed toward 0 instead of 1. The tilt strength \(\eta\) controls how far the unstable point moves.

The **asymmetric diffusion coefficient**:

\[ D(p) = 1 - \lambda_D \cdot \text{clamp}\!\left(\frac{-\phi(p)}{R_D}, \; 0, \; 1\right) \]

[7]

Full diffusion (\(D = 1\)) on the exterior. Suppressed diffusion (\(D = 1 - \lambda_D\)) on the interior. Prevents the Laplacian from smoothing/thinning the foreground.

The **confidence-gated effective time step**:

\[ \Delta t_{\text{eff}}(p) = \Delta t \cdot \text{clamp}\!\left(\frac{C(p) - \gamma_c}{1 - \gamma_c}, \; 0, \; 1\right) \]

[8]

Below confidence floor \(\gamma_c\), the PDE doesn't run. Ambiguous zones stay untouched.

### 4. Symbol Definitions

| Symbol | Definition | Range |
|--------|-----------|-------|
| \(\alpha^n(p)\) | Alpha at pixel \(p\) after \(n\) micro-iterations | \([0, 1]\) |
| \(\phi(p)\) | Signed distance; positive = exterior, negative = interior | \(\mathbb{R}\) |
| \(\varepsilon\) | Interface width parameter; controls steady-state sigmoid width | 1.0–2.0 |
| \(\eta\) | Exterior tilt strength; biases exterior alpha toward 0 | 0.0–0.25 |
| \(\lambda_D\) | Interior diffusion suppression factor | 0.0–0.9 |
| \(R_{\text{tilt}}\) | Tilt normalization radius (pixels) | 4.0–8.0 |
| \(R_D\) | Diffusion suppression radius (pixels) | 4.0–8.0 |
| \(\Delta t\) | Micro-iteration time step | 0.1–0.3 |
| \(N\) | Number of micro-iterations per frame | 3–8 |
| \(C(p)\) | Confidence map | \([0, 1]\) |
| \(\gamma_c\) | Confidence floor | 0.08–0.15 |
| \(\nabla^2\) | Discrete Laplacian via 3×3 kernel \([0,1,0;1,-4,1;0,1,0]\) | — |

### 5. Why BAR-lite Should Beat OSA-v2

OSA-v2 modifies velocity and then remaps. The remap step introduces interpolation diffusion that broadens the transition, and no velocity correction can undo post-remap broadening. BAR-lite operates entirely in-place — no remap, no interpolation, no displacement. The reaction term \(2\alpha(1-\alpha)(2\alpha-1)\) directly steepens the profile by pushing mid-band alpha values toward 0 or 1. The steady-state solution of the 1D Allen-Cahn equation is a hyperbolic tangent sigmoid whose width is controlled by \(\varepsilon\). A few micro-iterations move the profile partway toward this target shape without introducing any new diffusion artifact.[2][1]

### 6. Why It Should Reduce transition_band_mass

The reaction term is maximally active in the mid-band where \(\alpha \approx 0.3\text{--}0.7\). At \(\alpha = 0.5\), the magnitude \(|R| = \eta \cdot h\) (the cubic term vanishes). At \(\alpha = 0.3\), \(|R| \approx 0.168 + \eta \cdot h\). These mid-band pixels get pushed strongly toward their nearest well (0 or 1), which steepens the profile and removes the excess mass that makes the transition too gradual. The exterior tilt additionally biases mid-band exterior pixels toward 0, preferentially removing mass from the exterior half of the transition zone.

The diffusion term counteracts the reaction slightly (preventing infinite sharpness), but for \(\varepsilon = 1.5\) and 5 micro-iterations, the net effect is steepening. The diffusion only dominates in steady state at the interface center — far from steady state (where the current profile is), the reaction dominates.[3]

### 7. Why It Should Keep the outer_band_mass Win

On the outer band (\(\phi\) large positive), \(\alpha\) is already small (say 0.01–0.15). The reaction \(2\alpha(1-\alpha)(2\alpha-1)\) is negative for \(\alpha < 0.5\), meaning it pushes these values toward 0. The exterior tilt adds an additional downward push. So outer-band alpha values decrease or stay near zero. BAR-lite strictly reduces alpha on the outer band — it cannot increase it (the reaction for \(\alpha < 0.5\) with positive tilt is always \(\leq 0\)).

### 8. Why It Should Not Worsen temporal_lag_support

BAR-lite is applied after the temporal EMA step. It transforms alpha values in-place without any spatial displacement. Since no remap is involved, there is no interpolation-induced phase lag. The reaction term is deterministic and smooth — the same input alpha produces the same output, frame after frame. The confidence gate ensures that temporally unstable regions (low confidence) are left alone. The Laplacian term provides a tiny amount of spatial smoothing, which if anything reduces jitter rather than increasing lag.

The key difference from OSA: OSA moves alpha values spatially (via remap), which creates positional misalignment between frames (= lag). BAR-lite modifies alpha values locally (= no positional misalignment).

### 9. Core-Thinning Protection

Three layers of protection:

- **Interior diffusion suppression** (\(\lambda_D\)): On the interior (\(\phi < 0\)), the diffusion coefficient drops to \(1 - \lambda_D\). With \(\lambda_D = 0.6\), interior diffusion is only 40% of exterior. This prevents the Laplacian from smoothing foreground alpha downward.
- **Reaction fixed point at \(\alpha = 1\)**: For deep interior pixels where \(\alpha \approx 1\), the reaction \(2 \cdot 1 \cdot 0 \cdot 1 = 0\). The PDE has zero force at \(\alpha = 1\). It cannot thin the core.
- **Anchor pinning**: Pixels outside the narrow band retain their pre-BAR alpha values. BAR only runs inside the band.

### 10. Foldover / Instability Protection

The explicit Euler scheme for Allen-Cahn is stable under the CFL condition \(\Delta t \leq \varepsilon^2 h^2 / (2\varepsilon^2 + h^2)\). For \(h = 1\) (pixel grid) and \(\varepsilon = 1.5\): \(\Delta t \leq 1.5^2 \cdot 1 / (2 \cdot 1.5^2 + 1) = 2.25 / 5.5 \approx 0.409\). With \(\Delta t = 0.2\), the scheme is safely within the stability region with ~50% margin.[1][3]

Additional safeguards:
- Alpha is clamped to \([0, 1]\) after each micro-iteration
- The maximum per-iteration change is bounded by \(\Delta t \cdot (\varepsilon^2 \cdot 4 + |R_{\max}|) \approx 0.2 \cdot (2.25 \cdot 4 + 0.75) \approx 1.95\), but the clamp prevents runaway
- No spatial displacement → no remap foldover

### 11. Pseudocode

```python
def apply_bar_lite(self, alpha, alpha0, confidence, band_mask, config):
    """BAR-lite: Confidence-Gated Bistable Alpha Reaction."""
    phi = self._signed_distance  # positive = exterior
    
    # Precompute spatial maps (constant across micro-iterations)
    # Exterior tilt gate
    h = np.clip(phi / config.bar_R_tilt, 0.0, 1.0)
    
    # Asymmetric diffusion coefficient
    int_supp = np.clip(-phi / config.bar_R_D, 0.0, 1.0)
    D_map = 1.0 - config.bar_lambda_D * int_supp
    
    # Confidence-gated effective time step
    W_C = np.clip(
        (confidence - config.bar_gamma_c) / max(1.0 - config.bar_gamma_c, 1e-8),
        0.0, 1.0
    )
    dt_eff = config.bar_dt * W_C
    
    # Laplacian kernel
    lapl_k = np.array([[0, 1, 0],
                       [1,-4, 1],
                       [0, 1, 0]], dtype=np.float32)
    
    # Active mask = band only
    active = band_mask > 0
    eps2 = config.bar_epsilon ** 2
    
    a = alpha.copy()
    for _ in range(config.bar_n_iter):
        # Laplacian
        lap = cv2.filter2D(a, cv2.CV_32F, lapl_k)
        
        # Reaction: tilted double-well derivative
        reaction = 2.0 * a * (1.0 - a) * (2.0 * a - 1.0) - config.bar_eta * h
        
        # Update
        update = eps2 * D_map * lap - reaction
        a[active] = np.clip(
            a[active] + dt_eff[active] * update[active], 0.0, 1.0
        )
    
    # Preserve outside band
    result = alpha.copy()
    result[active] = a[active]
    
    # Floor: never below anchor floor
    result = np.maximum(result, config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0)
    
    return result
```

### 12. Insertion Point

```
... temporal EMA ...
... [skip OSA — disable it] ...
──► apply_bar_lite()      ← HERE: after EMA, before edge cleanup
... edge cleanup / despill ...
```

BAR-lite replaces OSA in this experiment. The temporal EMA has already stabilized the alpha field; BAR-lite reshapes its profile in-place.

### 13. Five-Pass Ablation

| Pass | Name | \(\varepsilon\) | \(\eta\) | \(\lambda_D\) | \(\Delta t\) | \(N\) | \(\gamma_c\) | Purpose |
|------|------|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|:---:|---------|
| P60 | `bar_lite_reaction_only` | 1.5 | 0.0 | 0.0 | 0.20 | 5 | 0.0 | Symmetric reaction + full diffusion, no gates. Measures raw profile steepening. Expect transition_band_mass drop, possible symmetric thinning. |
| P61 | `bar_lite_tilted` | 1.5 | 0.10 | 0.0 | 0.20 | 5 | 0.0 | Add exterior tilt. Expect asymmetric steepening — more reduction on exterior half. |
| P62 | `bar_lite_asymmetric` | 1.5 | 0.10 | 0.6 | 0.20 | 5 | 0.0 | Add interior diffusion suppression. Should prevent core thinning from P61. |
| P63 | `bar_lite_gated` | 1.5 | 0.10 | 0.6 | 0.20 | 5 | 0.12 | Add confidence gate. Should preserve temporal stability in ambiguous zones. **Expected sweet spot.** |
| P64 | `bar_lite_strong` | 1.2 | 0.15 | 0.7 | 0.18 | 8 | 0.10 | Narrower interface, more iterations, stronger tilt. Ceiling test. |

### What each pass tells you

- **P60**: Does the bistable reaction steepen the profile at all? If transition_band_mass doesn't drop, the reaction is too weak and \(\varepsilon\) must decrease or \(N\) must increase.
- **P61 vs P60**: Does the tilt asymmetry work? Compare interior vs exterior band mass changes.
- **P62 vs P61**: Does diffusion suppression prevent thinning? Check core_mean_alpha.
- **P63 vs P62**: Does confidence gating preserve temporal metrics? Check temporal_lag_support and temporal_jitter.
- **P64**: How hard can the PDE push before instability or over-sharpening?

### 14. Automatic Failure Metrics

```python
def bar_lite_metrics(alpha_bar, alpha_pre, alpha0, signed_d, band_mask,
                     confidence, R=6.0):
    """Comprehensive BAR-lite diagnostic metrics."""
    bp = band_mask > 0
    metrics = {}
    
    # 1. Transition band mass (MUST decrease)
    trans = bp & (np.abs(signed_d) < R)
    metrics['transition_band_mass'] = float(alpha_bar[trans].mean()) if trans.sum() > 0 else 0.0
    
    # 2. Outer band mass (MUST not increase)
    outer = bp & (signed_d > 0)
    metrics['outer_band_mass'] = float(alpha_bar[outer].sum()) / max(outer.sum(), 1) if outer.sum() > 0 else 0.0
    
    # 3. Core mean alpha (MUST not decrease)
    core = signed_d < -3.0
    metrics['core_mean_alpha'] = float(alpha_bar[core].mean()) if core.sum() > 0 else 0.0
    
    # 4. Per-iteration max change (stability monitor)
    max_delta = float(np.abs(alpha_bar - alpha_pre)[bp].max()) if bp.sum() > 0 else 0.0
    metrics['max_band_delta'] = max_delta
    
    # 5. Profile steepness: mean |d(alpha)/d(phi)| in transition zone
    grad_alpha = np.sqrt(cv2.Sobel(alpha_bar, cv2.CV_32F, 1, 0, ksize=3)**2 +
                         cv2.Sobel(alpha_bar, cv2.CV_32F, 0, 1, ksize=3)**2)
    metrics['profile_gradient'] = float(grad_alpha[trans].mean()) if trans.sum() > 0 else 0.0
    
    # 6. Turing artifact detector (high-freq oscillation in band)
    diff = alpha_bar - alpha_pre
    blur = cv2.GaussianBlur(diff, (5, 5), 1.0)
    hf = np.abs(diff - blur)
    metrics['turing_artifact'] = float(hf[bp].mean()) if bp.sum() > 0 else 0.0
    
    return metrics
```

**Pass/fail gates:**

| Metric | PASS | WARN | FAIL |
|--------|------|------|------|
| transition_band_mass | < 0.465 | 0.465–0.470 | ≥ 0.470 |
| outer_band_mass | < 0.155 | 0.155–0.162 | ≥ 0.162 |
| core_mean_alpha | ≥ 0.9925 | 0.9920–0.9925 | < 0.9920 |
| temporal_lag_support | < 0.275 | 0.275–0.282 | ≥ 0.282 |
| max_band_delta | < 0.15 | 0.15–0.25 | ≥ 0.25 |
| turing_artifact | < 0.005 | 0.005–0.010 | ≥ 0.010 |

```python
bar_lambda_D: float = 0.6         # Interior diffusion suppression [0-0.9]

bar_n_iter: int = 5               # Micro-iterations per frame

bar_R_D: float = 6.0              # Diffusion suppression radius

```

**`alpha_fix_2/pipeline.py`:**

```python
    alpha = self._apply_temporal_ema(alpha, ...)

        alpha = self.apply_bar_lite(alpha, alpha0, confidence, band_mask, config)
```

***

## Backup: OSA-v3-lite

### 1. Method Name

**OSA-v3-lite** — Temporal-Damped Advection with Post-Remap Anti-Diffusion

### 2. Failure Diagnosis

OSA's ramp broadening comes from the bilinear interpolation in `cv2.remap`. Each remap step is equivalent to convolving the profile with a small diffusion kernel. OSA-v3-lite keeps the temporal damping (the one thing that worked) and adds a **post-remap anti-diffusion step**: a single iteration of BFECC-style error correction that partially reverses the interpolation diffusion.[9][10]

### 3. Full Equations

Keep the temporally damped OSA velocity:

\[ v(p) = \kappa \cdot (\text{pivot} - \alpha) \cdot \text{envelope} \cdot (1 - \tau \cdot |\alpha - \alpha_{\text{prev}}|) \]

[11]

After remap, apply a one-step BFECC error estimate:

\[ \hat{\alpha} = \text{remap}(\alpha, v) \]

[12]

\[ \tilde{\alpha} = \text{remap}(\hat{\alpha}, -v) \]

[13]

\[ \alpha_{\text{error}} = \frac{\alpha - \tilde{\alpha}}{2} \]

[14]

\[ \alpha_{\text{corrected}} = \hat{\alpha} + \xi \cdot \alpha_{\text{error}} \cdot M(p) \]

[15]

where \(\xi \in [0, 1]\) is the error-correction strength and \(M(p)\) is a band mask that restricts correction to the transition zone.

### 4. Symbol Definitions

| Symbol | Definition | Range |
|--------|-----------|-------|
| \(v(p)\) | Temporally damped OSA velocity | — |
| \(\tau\) | Temporal disagreement damping strength | 0.3–0.4 |
| \(\hat{\alpha}\) | Forward-remapped alpha | \([0,1]\) |
| \(\tilde{\alpha}\) | Back-remapped alpha (round-trip) | \([0,1]\) |
| \(\alpha_{\text{error}}\) | BFECC error estimate | — |
| \(\xi\) | Error correction strength | 0.0–1.0 |
| \(M(p)\) | Transition-band mask | \(\{0, 1\}\) |

### 5. Why It Should Beat OSA-v2

The BFECC correction directly estimates and partially reverses the numerical diffusion introduced by the remap step. This is the exact mechanism causing ramp broadening. OSA-v2 tried to fix the velocity (divergence correction) but the problem was in the remap, not the velocity. OSA-v3-lite fixes the remap output directly.[9]

### 6. Why It Should Reduce transition_band_mass

The BFECC error \((\alpha - \tilde{\alpha})/2\) is positive where the remap diffused alpha outward and negative where it diffused inward. Adding it back sharpens the profile by undoing the diffusion — which is exactly the excess mid-band mass.

### 7. Why It Should Keep outer_band_mass Win

The temporal-damped velocity still pushes inward on the outer band. The BFECC correction only affects the mid-transition zone (gated by \(M\)).

### 8. Why It Should Not Worsen temporal_lag

The temporal damping \((1 - \tau \cdot |\alpha - \alpha_{\text{prev}}|)\) is retained. The BFECC correction is deterministic (same input → same output) and spatially smooth, adding no new temporal variance.

### 9. Core-Thinning Protection

\(M(p)\) restricts correction to the transition band only. Core pixels (\(\phi < -3\)) get zero correction.

### 10. Foldover / Instability Protection

BFECC with \(\xi \leq 1\) is unconditionally stable for linear advection. The clamp after correction prevents overshoots. The extra cost is exactly one additional remap call.[10]

### 11. Pseudocode

```python
def _apply_osa_v3_lite(self, alpha, alpha0, config):
    # Temporal-damped velocity
    disagree = np.abs(alpha - self._alpha_prev_warped)
    v = self._compute_osa_velocity(alpha, alpha0, config)
    v *= (1.0 - config.osa_tau * disagree)
    
    # Forward remap
    alpha_fwd = self._remap_along_normal(alpha, v, config)
    
    # BFECC error correction
    alpha_back = self._remap_along_normal(alpha_fwd, -v, config)
    error = (alpha - alpha_back) * 0.5
    
    # Apply correction in transition band only
    trans_mask = (np.abs(self._signed_distance) < config.osa_R) & (self._band_mask > 0)
    alpha_corrected = alpha_fwd.copy()
    alpha_corrected[trans_mask] += config.osa_xi * error[trans_mask]
    alpha_corrected = np.clip(alpha_corrected, 0.0, 1.0)
    
    # Floor
    return np.maximum(alpha_corrected, config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0)
```

### 12. Insertion Point

Same as current OSA: after temporal EMA, before edge cleanup.

### 13. Five-Pass Ablation

| Pass | Name | \(\tau\) | \(\xi\) | Purpose |
|------|------|:---:|:---:|---------|
| P65 | `osa_v3_lite_bfecc_only` | 0.0 | 0.5 | BFECC without temporal damping. Isolate anti-diffusion effect. |
| P66 | `osa_v3_lite_temporal_bfecc` | 0.35 | 0.5 | Combine both. Expected best. |
| P67 | `osa_v3_lite_strong_bfecc` | 0.35 | 0.8 | Stronger error correction. Check for ringing. |
| P68 | `osa_v3_lite_max_bfecc` | 0.35 | 1.0 | Full BFECC. If this rings, \(\xi\) needs to be lower. |
| P69 | `osa_v3_lite_conservative` | 0.40 | 0.3 | Strong damping, gentle correction. Lowest-risk variant. |

### 14. Automatic Failure Metrics

Same gates as BAR-lite, plus:

```python
def measure_bfecc_ringing(alpha_corrected, alpha_fwd, band_mask):
    """Check if BFECC introduced oscillations."""
    diff = alpha_corrected - alpha_fwd
    bp = band_mask > 0
    # Ringing = high-frequency sign changes
    sign_changes = np.abs(np.diff(np.sign(diff[bp])))
    return float(sign_changes.mean()) if len(sign_changes) > 0 else 0.0
```

### 15. Config Patch

```python
# --- OSA-v3-lite: Temporal-Damped Advection + BFECC ---
osa_v3_lite_enabled: bool = False  # backup, disabled by default
osa_tau: float = 0.35              # Temporal disagreement damping
osa_xi: float = 0.5               # BFECC error correction strength [0-1]
osa_R: float = 6.0                # Transition band radius for correction mask
```

***

## 16. Direct Ranking

**BAR-lite > OSA-v3-lite.**

BAR-lite attacks the root cause (profile shape) with a different mathematical tool (reaction-diffusion vs. advection). OSA-v3-lite is an incremental improvement to a method family that has shown consistent ramp-broadening across three iterations. Even with BFECC, the remap still introduces some diffusion that the error correction only partially reverses. BAR-lite has no remap at all.

## 17. Blunt Verdict

**Implement BAR-lite first** because:

- OSA has been tried three times and the transition_band_mass still goes up every time. The core mechanism (advect along normals → remap → interpolation broadening) is structural. BFECC can reduce the broadening but cannot eliminate it.
- BAR-lite is a fundamentally different approach: in-place transformation instead of spatial displacement. It directly steepens the profile through a bistable potential whose equilibrium IS a sharp sigmoid. No remap, no interpolation, no broadening mechanism.
- BAR-lite is actually simpler to implement: one Laplacian convolution + one elementwise reaction per iteration. No velocity field, no remap, no BFECC double-remap. Roughly 25 lines of core logic.
- The stability analysis is clean: \(\Delta t = 0.2 < 0.409\) = safe, with 50% margin.[3][1]
- If BAR-lite works, it opens a completely new direction. If OSA-v3-lite works, it's a marginal fix to a struggling family.

## 18. OSA Family Falsification Criterion

**The OSA family is dead if:** after implementing OSA-v3-lite with BFECC (\(\xi = 0.8\)) and temporal damping (\(\tau = 0.35\)), transition_band_mass still exceeds 0.470.

This would mean that even with second-order error correction on the remap, the advection-remap cycle cannot avoid broadening the transition. The structural cause (bilinear interpolation diffusion) is inherent to any `cv2.remap`-based approach, and no correction short of an exact inverse can fully undo it.

## 19. Why OSA Should Be Paused Now

Three data points tell a consistent story:

| | outer_band_mass Δ | transition_band_mass Δ | temporal_lag Δ |
|---|:---:|:---:|:---:|
| OSA v1 | −0.016 | +0.010 | +0.012 |
| OSA v2 | −0.012 | +0.005 | +0.008 |
| OSA v2 temporal | −0.011 | +0.004 | +0.007 |

Every OSA variant trades transition_band_mass for outer_band_mass. The ratio is improving (the broadening is getting smaller relative to the compression) but it has never crossed zero. The temporal damping was the only win, and it addresses lag, not broadening.

Meanwhile, BAR-lite has never been tried. It uses a completely different mathematical mechanism. It has zero structural reason to broaden the transition (no remap). Its failure modes (over-sharpening, instability) are well-understood from PDE theory and easy to detect with the proposed metrics. The worst case — BAR-lite does nothing — costs one evening and definitively answers whether profile-shape correction via bistable reaction is viable. The best case — BAR-lite reduces transition_band_mass without increasing lag — opens a new method family that bypasses the OSA bottleneck entirely.[1][3]

Pause OSA. Run BAR-lite. If it fails, OSA-v3-lite with BFECC is sitting ready as the fallback.

The full decision with all 20 deliverables is in the attached report. Here's the short version:

**Primary: BAR-lite. Backup: OSA-v3-lite.**

The data is clear. OSA has been tried three times and transition_band_mass goes up every time (+0.010, +0.005, +0.004). The broadening is structural — `cv2.remap` bilinear interpolation IS a diffusion kernel, and no velocity correction can undo post-remap diffusion. Temporal damping helped lag but doesn't touch broadening.

BAR-lite takes a fundamentally different approach: no remap, no displacement, no interpolation. A tilted Allen-Cahn bistable reaction transforms alpha values **in-place**, pushing mid-band values toward 0 or 1 through a double-well potential whose equilibrium is a steep sigmoid. The exterior tilt biases the exterior half toward zero. Interior diffusion suppression protects the foreground. Confidence gating preserves temporal stability. Explicit Euler is stable at \(\Delta t = 0.2\) with 50% CFL margin. [aimspress](https://www.aimspress.com/aimspress-data/math/2024/12/PDF/math-09-12-1641.pdf)

It's also simpler to code: one `filter2D` + one elementwise reaction per iteration, ~25 lines of core logic, no velocity field, no remap. Five-pass ablation from P60 (raw reaction) through P64 (aggressive) isolates each component cleanly.

OSA-v3-lite (BFECC anti-diffusion on the remap output) is the backup if BAR-lite fails, and also serves as the falsification test: if BFECC at \(\xi = 0.8\) still can't prevent transition_band_mass > 0.470, the OSA family is dead.

# Technical Judge Report: BAR-lite vs OSA-v3-lite

Two proposals are under review from the previous conversation turn. Both target the same problem: pass_15's transition_band_mass is 0.4694, and every OSA variant has made it worse (0.4795, 0.4746, 0.4737). The proposals are evaluated strictly against the measured sandbox history.

***

## Proposal A: BAR-lite (Confidence-Gated Bistable Alpha Reaction)

### 1. Short name
BAR-lite

### 2. Does it react to measured history?
**Yes, strongly.** The proposal explicitly cites the three OSA data points showing transition_band_mass increases (+0.010, +0.005, +0.004), correctly identifies the trend as structural to the remap mechanism, and proposes an entirely different mathematical family (reaction-diffusion) that avoids remap entirely. It correctly notes that temporal damping was the only useful component of OSA. It correctly identifies the profile-shape problem (too gradual in mid-band) as distinct from the outer-band tail problem. This is the most history-aware proposal in the conversation.

### 3. Specific failure mode addressed
Transition-zone profile shape: the alpha profile between \(\phi = -3\) and \(\phi = +5\) is approximately linear rather than sigmoid. OSA cannot reshape this because `cv2.remap` bilinear interpolation acts as a diffusion kernel that widens the profile. BAR-lite applies an in-place bistable reaction that drives mid-band alpha values toward their nearest stable state (0 or 1), steepening the profile without any spatial displacement.[1]

### 4. Is the math coherent?
**Yes, with minor caveats.** The Allen-Cahn equation with tilted double-well potential is standard PDE theory. The reaction term \(2\alpha(1-\alpha)(2\alpha-1) - \eta \cdot h(\phi)\) has the correct three fixed points, correct sign of the tilt, and the exterior tilt gate \(h = \text{clamp}(\phi/R, 0, 1)\) correctly uses the repo's sign convention (\(\phi > 0\) = outside). The asymmetric diffusion suppression using \(\text{clamp}(-\phi/R, 0, 1)\) also correctly targets the interior. The CFL condition is stated as \(\Delta t \leq \varepsilon^2 / (2\varepsilon^2 + 1) \approx 0.409\) for \(\varepsilon = 1.5, h = 1\), with the proposed \(\Delta t = 0.2\) safely within bounds.[2][3]

**Caveat 1:** The CFL condition cited is for the standard Allen-Cahn without the asymmetric diffusion modification. The interior suppression (\(D < 1\)) makes the condition less restrictive on the interior, so this is conservative — safe.

**Caveat 2:** The tilt term \(-\eta \cdot h\) adds a constant forcing that technically makes the reaction not purely a double-well derivative. This doesn't break stability but shifts the fixed points. For \(\eta = 0.10\), the unstable fixed point moves from 0.5 to approximately 0.475 on the exterior — a modest shift, not destabilizing.

### 5. Sign errors, stability errors, or architectural mismatches?
**No sign errors.** The signed distance convention is correctly applied throughout (positive = outside, negative = inside). The Laplacian kernel \([0,1,0;1,-4,1;0,1,0]\) is standard. The clamp to  after each iteration prevents runaway. The confidence gate uses the existing `confidence` map. The band mask uses the existing `band_mask`. The anchor floor uses the existing `cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor`.[4]

**One architectural question:** The proposal says BAR-lite "replaces OSA" in the experiment. This is correct for a clean ablation. But the insertion point "after EMA, before edge cleanup" is also where OSA currently sits, so no pipeline reordering is needed — just swap the call.

### 6. Implementable tonight?
**Yes.** The core is ~25 lines: one `cv2.filter2D` + one elementwise reaction per iteration, looped 5 times. All inputs exist in the pipeline (`signed_distance`, `confidence`, `band_mask`, `alpha0`). No new helper functions needed beyond the BAR-lite function itself. The config additions are 8 floats + 1 int. Estimated implementation time: 30–45 minutes including the 5-pass ablation runner.

### 7. Preserves outer-band mass win?
**Yes, by construction.** On the outer band (\(\phi > 0\), \(\alpha < 0.5\)), the reaction \(2\alpha(1-\alpha)(2\alpha-1)\) is negative (pushes toward 0), and the tilt \(-\eta \cdot h\) adds more downward push. BAR-lite strictly reduces alpha in the outer band. It cannot increase outer-band mass. However, the magnitude of reduction is uncertain — the reaction term is weaker for small \(\alpha\) values (approaching 0, the reaction \(\approx 0\)) so the outer-band effect may be small compared to OSA's direct advection. This is acceptable — the goal is to not lose the pass_15 baseline, not to beat OSA on outer-band specifically.

### 8. Believable mechanism for transition_band_mass reduction?
**Yes — this is the proposal's strongest point.** The double-well potential is maximally active at mid-band alpha values (0.2–0.8). At \(\alpha = 0.5\), the cubic reaction term is zero but the tilt fires. At \(\alpha = 0.3\), \(|R| \approx 0.168 + \eta \cdot h\). These mid-band pixels are exactly where transition_band_mass lives. The reaction pushes them toward 0 or 1, steepening the profile. This directly addresses the "too gradual slope" that constitutes excess transition mass. No remap → no interpolation broadening → no mechanism to re-widen what the reaction just steepened.

The Allen-Cahn steady state IS a hyperbolic tangent sigmoid — the ideal profile shape. Even 5 micro-iterations won't reach steady state, but the trajectory is toward the correct target.[5][6]

### 9. Believable mechanism for temporal_lag_support safety?
**Mostly yes.** No remap = no positional displacement = no interpolation-induced phase lag. The reaction is purely local and deterministic. The confidence gate suppresses the PDE in low-confidence zones where temporal instability originates.

**One concern:** The Laplacian term IS a spatial operation that could introduce small temporal variance if the alpha field has frame-to-frame noise that the EMA didn't fully suppress. But the Laplacian is multiplied by \(\varepsilon^2 \cdot D\) and then by \(\Delta t_{\text{eff}}\), so the total spatial smoothing per iteration is at most \(\varepsilon^2 \cdot \Delta t = 0.45\) px², spread over 5 iterations = 2.25 px² cumulative. This is comparable to a very mild Gaussian blur (\(\sigma \approx 1.1\) px) — unlikely to cause measurable lag increase.

### 10. Main hidden risk
**Over-sharpening on soft foreground edges.** If a legitimate foreground feature (hair, motion blur, semi-transparency) has alpha values in the 0.3–0.7 range within the narrow band, the bistable reaction will try to push them toward 0 or 1. The confidence gate provides some protection (these features often have low confidence), but if confidence happens to be moderate, the PDE will treat legitimate soft detail as "transition zone to be steepened." The `soft_edge_fraction` metric (currently 0.0603) should be monitored for catastrophic drop.

A secondary risk is that 5 iterations at \(\Delta t = 0.2\) may be too few to produce a measurable effect on 6-pixel-wide transition zones. The total evolution time is \(T = 5 \times 0.2 = 1.0\), and the Allen-Cahn relaxation timescale is \(\sim \varepsilon^2 = 2.25\). So the profile moves about 44% of the way toward steady state — enough to be measurable, but the ablation's P60 (raw reaction, no gates) will test this.

### 11. Verdict
**Implement now.**

***

## Proposal B: OSA-v3-lite (Temporal-Damped Advection + BFECC)

### 1. Short name
OSA-v3-lite

### 2. Does it react to measured history?
**Partially.** The proposal correctly identifies that remap interpolation broadens the transition (explaining the +0.010/+0.005/+0.004 pattern). It correctly identifies temporal damping as the one useful component. However, it then proposes to fix the remap with BFECC error correction — which is still within the OSA/remap family that has failed three times. The proposal acknowledges this: "the remap still introduces some diffusion that the error correction only partially reverses." This is honest but not encouraging.

### 3. Specific failure mode addressed
Remap-induced interpolation diffusion. BFECC estimates the round-trip error by advecting forward and backward, then compensates. This is the right tool for reducing advection diffusion in fluid simulation.[7][8]

### 4. Is the math coherent?
**Yes.** BFECC is well-established: forward advect \(\hat{\alpha} = \text{remap}(\alpha, v)\), backward advect \(\tilde{\alpha} = \text{remap}(\hat{\alpha}, -v)\), error = \((\alpha - \tilde{\alpha})/2\), corrected = \(\hat{\alpha} + \xi \cdot \text{error}\)[9][10]. For linear advection, this lifts first-order semi-Lagrangian to second-order accuracy. The temporal damping \((1 - \tau \cdot |\alpha - \alpha_{\text{prev}}|)\) is the correct formulation (disagreement-based, not the inverted lag_map from the earlier OSA-v2 bug).

### 5. Sign errors, stability errors, or architectural mismatches?
**No sign errors.** The BFECC scheme uses the same velocity \(v\) and its negation \(-v\) — sign-symmetric. The transition band mask \(M(p)\) restricts correction to \(|\phi| < R\). The \(\xi\) parameter clamps the correction strength.

**One concern:** BFECC for nonlinear advection can introduce oscillations near sharp gradients. The original BFECC paper recommends a limiting step to clamp the corrected value within the original local range. The proposal does not include a limiter — it relies on the \(\xi\) parameter and band mask instead. This may be acceptable for \(\xi \leq 0.5\), but at \(\xi = 0.8\) (P67) or \(\xi = 1.0\) (P68), ringing is likely.[11]

**Architectural note:** The proposal requires a `_remap_along_normal` function that accepts negative velocity. This should already exist in the OSA codebase (just negate the displacement map), but worth verifying.

### 6. Implementable tonight?
**Yes, if OSA infrastructure exists.** The core addition is one extra remap call (backward) + elementwise error computation + masked addition. ~15 lines on top of existing OSA code. However, if OSA is being disabled for BAR-lite, the OSA infrastructure must be re-enabled for this experiment. Estimated: 20–30 minutes.

### 7. Preserves outer-band mass win?
**Yes.** The forward remap is identical to current OSA (which achieves the outer-band win). BFECC only corrects the mid-band diffusion — it shouldn't affect the outer-band push.

### 8. Believable mechanism for transition_band_mass reduction?
**Weak-to-moderate.** BFECC can partially reverse interpolation broadening, but it cannot fully eliminate it. The error estimate \((\alpha - \tilde{\alpha})/2\) captures first-order diffusion error. For bilinear interpolation on a 1-pixel grid, the diffusion coefficient is approximately \(h^2/12 \approx 0.083\) per remap step. BFECC reduces this by a factor related to \(\xi\), but does not zero it out. The net broadening per frame would go from ~0.083 to ~0.083 \(\times (1 - \xi)\).[9]

With \(\xi = 0.5\), the broadening drops by half. Over multiple frames, the cumulative broadening could still exceed the compression from advection. The proposal is honest about this limitation.

Critically: **the measured data shows transition_band_mass rising even after temporal damping (pass_59: 0.4737 vs baseline 0.4694).** BFECC would need to reverse a +0.0043 delta. Given that the per-frame broadening is small and BFECC partially corrects it, the net improvement might be on the order of 0.001–0.002 — possibly not enough to cross below baseline.

### 9. Believable mechanism for temporal_lag_support safety?
**Yes.** Temporal damping is retained. BFECC is deterministic (same input → same correction). The extra remap (backward pass) introduces no new temporal information — it uses the same velocity field.

### 10. Main hidden risk
**BFECC oscillations near the \(\phi = 0\) boundary.** The alpha profile has its steepest gradient at the boundary. BFECC error correction can overshoot near gradients, creating oscillating alpha values that look like chatter. The proposal notes this risk for \(\xi \geq 0.8\) but the effect may appear even at \(\xi = 0.5\) if the profile is steep enough. Without a BFECC limiter, this is a real risk.[11]

A secondary risk is that the extra remap call doubles the interpolation cost — both forward and backward passes contribute diffusion, and the error estimate only captures the first-order term. Higher-order diffusion from the double-remap may partially offset the correction.

### 11. Verdict
**Keep as backup.**

***

## Score Table

| Criterion | BAR-lite | OSA-v3-lite |
|-----------|:---:|:---:|
| **History awareness** — reacts to measured pass_51/55/59 data | 9 | 6 |
| **Mathematical coherence** — equations are correct, bounded, stable | 8 | 8 |
| **Sandbox fit** — uses existing helpers, correct conventions, tonight-ready | 9 | 7 |
| **Expected outer-band win** — preserves or improves pass_15 outer_band_mass | 6 | 8 |
| **Expected ramp-width improvement** — reduces transition_band_mass below 0.4694 | 8 | 4 |
| **Expected temporal safety** — avoids worsening temporal_lag_support | 8 | 7 |
| **Implementation clarity** — pseudocode is complete, insertion point is clear | 9 | 8 |
| **Overall priority** | **8.1** | **6.9** |

### Score Justifications

**BAR-lite scores high on history awareness (9)** because it explicitly diagnoses the structural remap-broadening problem across three data points and proposes an entirely different mathematical family to avoid it. It scores high on ramp-width improvement (8) because the bistable reaction mechanism directly targets mid-band alpha values, which is where transition_band_mass lives. It loses a point on outer-band (6) because the reaction term is weak near \(\alpha = 0\) — BAR-lite probably won't *improve* outer-band mass, only *not worsen* it. It loses a point on math coherence (8) for the CFL condition being approximate with the asymmetric diffusion modification, though this is conservative (safe).

**OSA-v3-lite scores lower on history awareness (6)** because it proposes a fourth attempt in the same remap-based family that has failed three times. The BFECC idea is sound but the proposal acknowledges it can only partially fix the broadening. It scores well on outer-band (8) because it retains the exact OSA mechanism that produced the outer-band win. It scores poorly on ramp-width (4) because the measured broadening delta (+0.0043) is likely larger than what partial BFECC correction can reverse. It loses a point on sandbox fit (7) because it requires OSA infrastructure to be active, which conflicts with BAR-lite testing.

***

## 12. Final Ranking

1. **BAR-lite** — Different family, directly targets the failure mode, no remap, history-aware.
2. **OSA-v3-lite** — Sound incremental fix, but fourth try in a struggling family.

***

## 13. Blunt Implementation Verdict

**Code next: BAR-lite.**
The remap family has been tried three times and transition_band_mass went up every time. The BFECC correction is theoretically partial (it reduces interpolation diffusion but cannot eliminate it), and the measured broadening delta (+0.0043 even with temporal damping) may exceed what partial BFECC correction can reverse. BAR-lite is a clean break: no remap, no interpolation, no broadening mechanism. Its core loop is 25 lines. It should take 30–45 minutes to implement and run the 5-pass ablation.[9]

**Keep as backup: OSA-v3-lite.**
If BAR-lite is a no-op (reaction too weak at 5 iterations) or destroys soft edges, OSA-v3-lite is ready. The BFECC addition is ~15 lines on top of existing OSA. It should be coded only if BAR-lite P60 (raw reaction) shows no measurable transition_band_mass change.

**Rejected: None.**
Both proposals are mathematically sound and implementable. Neither is rejected, but OSA-v3-lite should only be run if BAR-lite fails.

***

## 14. Falsification Criterion for BAR-lite

**BAR-lite is dead if:** after P64 (`bar_lite_strong`: \(\varepsilon = 1.2\), \(\eta = 0.15\), \(\lambda_D = 0.7\), \(\Delta t = 0.18\), \(N = 8\), \(\gamma_c = 0.10\)), transition_band_mass is still ≥ 0.468.

This would mean: even with 8 micro-iterations, stronger tilt, narrower interface width, and lower confidence floor, the bistable reaction cannot steepen the profile enough to measurably reduce mid-band mass. The implication would be that the excess transition mass is not a profile-shape problem but something else — possibly incorrect signed-distance computation, or the EMA itself locking in a wide profile that the reaction cannot overcome in a single frame's worth of evolution.

If this happens, the next direction is **not** more BAR iterations (diminishing returns from the CFL constraint) but rather investigating whether the transition-zone width is set upstream by the EMA or the confidence map, and the post-EMA correction is attacking the wrong stage of the pipeline.

***

## 15. Reasoned Conclusion

Three iterations of OSA (v1, v2, temporal-only) have produced a consistent empirical pattern: outer-band mass drops, but transition-band mass rises by +0.004 to +0.010 per variant, and temporal lag increases. The best OSA result (pass_59) still has transition_band_mass 0.0043 above baseline, and the improvement from v1 to v2 to temporal-only is flattening. BFECC could reduce the remap-induced broadening by an estimated 40–60%, but that maps to a transition_band_mass improvement of roughly 0.002–0.003 — likely insufficient to cross below baseline. BAR-lite is the correct next experiment because it attacks mid-band alpha values directly through a bistable reaction whose equilibrium is a steep sigmoid, requires no remap, introduces no interpolation broadening, and is implementable in 25 lines. The main risk — over-sharpening soft edges — is detectable by monitoring `soft_edge_fraction` and addressable by reducing \(\eta\) or increasing \(\varepsilon\). The ablation plan (P60–P64) cleanly isolates each component. If BAR-lite fails the falsification criterion after all 5 passes, the conclusion is that the excess transition mass originates upstream of the post-EMA stage, and both BAR and OSA families should be paused in favor of investigating the EMA or confidence map themselves.

Short answer:
Implement two explicit modes: SUBJECT (island) and OVERLAY (donut), sharing some primitives but with different alpha0 construction and refinement. Code OVERLAY multi-hole flood mode v2 next, with SUBJECT bright-edge clamp v1 as backup.

1. Topology diagnosis
SUBJECT / ISLAND: single connected foreground component, background is “infinite” outside; alpha transitions from 1 (subject) to 0 (outside) across a single outer boundary. White halos are local premultiplied contamination on that one boundary, not a topology error.

OVERLAY / DONUT: foreground is a frame with interior holes (center gameplay window, chat window). Background must be 0 inside those holes while staying 1 on the frame. The main failure so far was treating the entire frame as foreground (no internal holes), so display capture is hidden.

Different math: subject wants one exterior interface shaped correctly, overlay wants multiple interior components cut out robustly. Trying to handle both with the same topology assumptions (single foreground blob) is what broke overlays.

2. Architecture choice
Choice: two explicit extraction modes.

SUBJECT mode: current v2 pipeline + subject-specific halo refinement.

OVERLAY mode: center/chat-hole extraction + overlay-specific refinement.

Justification:

Topology, metric goals, and failure modes are different. A single unified topology-aware solver would be more complex and harder to debug tonight.

The repo already has a separate “center-hole flood” success; codifying that as OVERLAY mode is low risk and immediately valuable (26% nonzero alpha success).

Mode selection can be driven by config or simple heuristics (e.g., asset type in batch manifest).

3. SUBJECT branch – next refinement
Goal: fix white halo / bright-edge mass on white backgrounds without OSA/BAR-style full-ramp manipulation.

Core idea: “Bright-Edge Biased Clamp” (BEBC)
Do NOT advect or PDE-evolve alpha.

Instead, detect high-luma, background-colored pixels in the narrow band on the exterior side, and locally clamp alpha toward 0, with strong protection on the interior side (to avoid thinning).

4. OVERLAY branch – robust multi-hole extraction
Goal: robustly cut out center gameplay window and chat window(s), while preserving dark decorative frame and avoiding leaks through other dark regions.

Core idea: “Flood-Gated Multi-Hole Overlay” (FGMO)
Use seeded flood-fill in alpha space, gated by image edges and darkness, then invert to get frame.

ov

otherwise

This keeps frame crisp while allowing controlled feathering at the inner edges.

6. Pseudocode – SUBJECT BEBC
python
def _subject_refine_bebc(self, alpha, alpha0, frame_bgr, phi, conf, config):
    # Narrow band masks
    band = np.abs(phi) <= config.subj_band_radius
    ext = (phi > 0) & band

    # RGB -> [0,1]
    frame = frame_bgr.astype(np.float32) / 255.0

    # Estimate background color b as median of low-alpha region
    low_alpha_mask = alpha0 < 0.1
    if np.any(low_alpha_mask):
        b = np.median(frame[low_alpha_mask], axis=0)
    else:
        b = np.array([1.0, 1.0, 1.0], dtype=np.float32)

    # Luma
    Y = 0.2126 * frame[...,0] + 0.7152 * frame[...,1] + 0.0722 * frame[...,2]
    # Color distance to background
    diff = frame - b[None,None,:]
    delta_b = np.linalg.norm(diff, axis=-1)

    # Exterior bright-background score
    sY = np.clip(Y - config.subj_bebc_ty, 0.0, 1.0)
    sb = np.clip(config.subj_bebc_tb - delta_b, 0.0, 1.0)
    s_ext = config.subj_bebc_sigma_y * sY + config.subj_bebc_sigma_b * sb

    d = np.abs(phi)
    gauss_d = np.exp(-0.5 * (d / config.subj_bebc_sigma_d) ** 2)

    g_ext = gauss_d * s_ext * conf
    g_ext = np.clip(g_ext, 0.0, 1.0)

    alpha_new = alpha.copy()
    alpha_new[ext] *= (1.0 - config.subj_bebc_lambda_ext * g_ext[ext])

    # Anchor floor
    alpha_floor = self.config.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor
    alpha_new = np.maximum(alpha_new, alpha_floor * alpha0)

    # Clip
    alpha_new = np.clip(alpha_new, 0.0, 1.0)
    return alpha_new
7. Pseudocode – OVERLAY FGMO
python
def _overlay_extract_multi_hole(self, alpha0, frame_bgr, config):
    H, W = alpha0.shape

    # Raw foreground mask
    m_raw = alpha0 > config.overlay_t_alpha0

    # Luma and darkness
    frame = frame_bgr.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
    Y = 0.2126 * frame[...,0] + 0.7152 * frame[...,1] + 0.0722 * frame[...,2]
    dark = 1.0 - Y
    m_dark = dark > config.overlay_t_dark

    # Edge mask
    gray = cv2.cvtColor(frame_bgr, cv2.COLOR_BGR2GRAY)
    edges = cv2.Canny(gray,
                      config.overlay_edge_canny_low,
                      config.overlay_edge_canny_high)
    m_edge = edges > 0

    # Block mask: edges + dark foreground
    m_block = m_edge | (m_dark & m_raw)

    # Flood seeds
    cx, cy = W // 2, H // 2
    kx = config.overlay_center_kx
    ky = config.overlay_center_ky
    center_rect = (slice(int(cy - ky * H), int(cy + ky * H)),
                   slice(int(cx - kx * W), int(cx + kx * W)))
    seed_center = np.zeros_like(alpha0, dtype=bool)
    seed_center[center_rect] = True

    kx_chat = config.overlay_chat_kx
    kh_chat = config.overlay_chat_kh
    x_chat = int(W * (1.0 - kx_chat))
    y1_chat = int(cy - kh_chat * H)
    y2_chat = int(cy + kh_chat * H)
    seed_chat = np.zeros_like(alpha0, dtype=bool)
    seed_chat[y1_chat:y2_chat, x_chat:W] = True

    # Flood function over low-alpha & not blocked
    def flood_from_seed(seed_mask):
        visited = np.zeros_like(alpha0, dtype=bool)
        q = collections.deque()
        ys, xs = np.where(seed_mask)
        for y, x in zip(ys, xs):
            if (0 <= x < W) and (0 <= y < H):
                if alpha0[y, x] < config.overlay_t_alpha0 and not m_block[y, x]:
                    visited[y, x] = True
                    q.append((y, x))
        while q:
            y, x = q.popleft()
            for dy, dx in ((1,0),(-1,0),(0,1),(0,-1)):
                ny, nx = y+dy, x+dx
                if (0 <= nx < W) and (0 <= ny < H):
                    if not visited[ny, nx] and not m_block[ny, nx] and alpha0[ny, nx] < config.overlay_t_alpha0:
                        visited[ny, nx] = True
                        q.append((ny, nx))
        return visited

    f_center = flood_from_seed(seed_center)
    f_chat   = flood_from_seed(seed_chat)

    # Frame mask
    m_frame = m_raw & ~(f_center | f_chat)

    # Optional feathering
    frame_uint8 = (m_frame.astype(np.uint8) * 255)
    dist_inside = cv2.distanceTransform(frame_uint8, cv2.DIST_L2, 3)
    dist_outside = cv2.distanceTransform(255 - frame_uint8, cv2.DIST_L2, 3)
    dist = np.where(m_frame, dist_outside, dist_inside)

    alpha_overlay = np.zeros_like(alpha0, dtype=np.float32)
    # Hard core
    alpha_overlay[m_frame & (dist <= 0.5)] = 1.0
    # Feather zone
    feather = (dist > 0.5) & (dist <= config.overlay_r_ov)
    alpha_overlay[feather] = np.exp(-0.5 * ((dist[feather] - 0.5) / config.overlay_sigma_ov) ** 2)

    return np.clip(alpha_overlay, 0.0, 1.0)
Pipeline insertion: in OVERLAY mode, skip the usual post-EMA subject refinement and use _overlay_extract_multi_hole to overwrite alpha.

10. Automatic failure metrics
SUBJECT mode
Compute on subject clips:

Halo failure:

bright_outer_mass: sum of α in pixels with phi>0, band, Y>0.9, delta_b<0.2.
Fail if bright_outer_mass >= baseline + 2%.

Thinning failure:

core_mean_alpha < 0.9920 (baseline ~0.9931).

Ramp relapse:

transition_band_mass > baseline + 0.003 (i.e. > 0.4724).

Temporal lag regression:

temporal_lag_support > baseline + 0.010 (i.e. > 0.2791).

Soft-edge collapse:

soft_edge_fraction < baseline - 0.010 (i.e. < 0.0503).

OVERLAY mode
Compute on overlay clips with known gameplay/chat regions (rects):

Center-hole failure:

center_mean_alpha > 0.05 (should be near 0).

Chat-hole failure:

if chat present: chat_mean_alpha > 0.05.

Frame loss:

frame_mean_alpha < 0.98 on the outer frame region.

Leak-through elsewhere:

other_dark_leak_fraction > 0.02 (nonzero alpha where underlying display capture should be blocked).

Overfill regression:

global_nonzero_fraction > 0.35 (we expect ~0.26 or lower vs 0.999 baseline).
