# Alpha Fix Dual-Topology Implementation Plan

## Topology Diagnosis

Subject/island and overlay/donut are fundamentally different extraction problems that share almost no mathematical structure beyond the compositing equation \(I = \alpha F + (1-\alpha) B\).[1][2]

**Subject / Island topology** has a single connected foreground component surrounded by infinite background. The signed distance field has one zero-crossing. The entire pipeline — anchor matte, confidence map, narrow band, temporal EMA — assumes this topology. The remaining failure is a **boundary-local** problem: excess alpha mass on the exterior side of that single boundary, caused by background-colored (typically bright/white) pixels retaining nonzero alpha after EMA stabilization. The OSA and BAR experiments confirmed this is a profile-shape issue in a 4–8 px transition band. The problem is mathematically analogous to color spill in chroma keying: the background color "leaks" into the foreground edge through the compositing equation.[3][4]

**Overlay / Donut topology** has foreground that forms a frame with one or more interior holes. The signed distance field has **multiple** zero-crossings (outer frame boundary + inner hole boundaries). The current pipeline's single-blob assumption treats the entire frame as foreground because the anchor matte correctly identifies high-alpha decorative pixels everywhere — there is no "background" in the traditional sense. The measured breakthrough (99.99% → 26.0% nonzero) came from seeded flood-fill that explicitly carved interior holes. The remaining failures (imperfect chat-hole extraction, dark-region leak-through) are topology-extraction problems, not boundary-refinement problems.

These require different algorithms: subject needs **boundary profile correction**, overlay needs **interior hole carving + frame preservation**.

## Architecture Decision

**Two explicit extraction modes**, not a unified topology-aware framework.

Justification:

- The algorithms share almost no logic. Subject mode refines a narrow band around one boundary; overlay mode carves interior regions from a frame mask.
- A unified framework would need automatic topology detection, which is itself a research problem that would delay both branches.
- The repo already has a working center-hole flood. Codifying it as overlay mode is near-zero risk.
- Mode selection is trivially driven by a config flag or batch manifest tag. Users know whether their asset is a subject or an overlay.
- Debugging and ablation are cleaner with separate code paths.

```
config.mode = "subject"  # or "overlay"
```

## Subject Branch: Luma-Weighted Inverse-Premultiply Clamp (LIPC)

### Diagnosis

The white halo on subject assets is **not** a ramp-width problem (OSA/BAR territory). It is a **color contamination** problem. In compressed video on white backgrounds, the compositing equation means that pixels near the boundary with \(\alpha \approx 0.1\text{--}0.3\) have RGB values close to the background white, because \(I \approx 0.1 F + 0.9 B \approx B\) when \(B\) is white. The current pipeline assigns nonzero alpha to these pixels because the LAB Mahalanobis distance from background is small but nonzero (compression noise), and the EMA locks that alpha in.[5][6]

OSA failed because it tried to advect these pixels inward (broadening the ramp). BAR failed because it tried to steepen the profile globally (but the reaction term is weak at \(\alpha \approx 0.1\)). Neither attacked the root cause: **these pixels have high alpha relative to their actual foreground content**.

### Core Idea

The inverse compositing equation gives the foreground estimate \(\hat{F} = (I - (1-\alpha)B) / \alpha\). For halo pixels, \(\hat{F}\) will be near-white or even out-of-gamut (values > 1.0), because \(\alpha\) is too high for the actual foreground contribution. LIPC uses this signal: compute the estimated foreground luma, and if it's suspiciously close to the background, reduce alpha.[7][8]

This directly targets the color-contamination mechanism instead of manipulating the alpha profile shape.

### Mathematical Formulation

Let:

- \(I(p) \in [0,1]^3\) — RGB frame at pixel \(p\), normalized
- \(B \in [0,1]^3\) — estimated background color (median of \(\alpha_0 < 0.05\) pixels, or fallback \([1,1,1]\))
- \(\alpha(p) \in [0,1]\) — post-EMA alpha
- \(\alpha_0(p)\) — anchor matte
- \(\phi(p)\) — signed distance (\(>0\) outside, \(<0\) inside)
- \(R_s\) — subject band radius (px)
- \(E_{\text{out}}(p) = [\phi(p) > 0] \land [|\phi(p)| \le R_s]\) — exterior band mask

**Step 1: Estimate foreground color**

For each pixel in the exterior band where \(\alpha(p) > \alpha_{\min}\):

\[
\hat{F}(p) = \frac{I(p) - (1 - \alpha(p)) \cdot B}{\alpha(p)}
\] [9]

Clamp \(\hat{F}\) to \([0, 2]\) (allow slight out-of-gamut for detection).

**Step 2: Compute foreground-background similarity**

\[
Y_F(p) = 0.2126 \hat{F}_R + 0.7152 \hat{F}_G + 0.0722 \hat{F}_B
\] [10]

\[
\Delta_F(p) = \|\hat{F}(p) - B\|_2
\] [11]

**Step 3: Compute halo score**

\[
h(p) = \text{clamp}\left(\frac{T_\Delta - \Delta_F(p)}{T_\Delta}, 0, 1\right) \cdot \text{clamp}\left(\frac{Y_F(p) - T_Y}{1 - T_Y}, 0, 1\right)
\] [12]

where \(T_\Delta\) is a color-distance threshold (e.g., 0.35) and \(T_Y\) is a luma threshold (e.g., 0.80). The halo score is high when the estimated foreground is both close to the background color AND bright.

**Step 4: Distance-weighted exterior clamp**

\[
w(p) = \exp\!\left(-\frac{\phi(p)^2}{2\sigma_d^2}\right)
\] [13]

(Gaussian centered at boundary, \(\sigma_d \approx 2.5\) px.)

**Step 5: Alpha reduction**

\[
\alpha'(p) = \alpha(p) \cdot (1 - \lambda \cdot h(p) \cdot w(p) \cdot c(p))
\] [14]

where \(\lambda \in (0,1]\) is the clamp strength and \(c(p)\) is the existing confidence map.

**Step 6: Floor + clip**

\[
\alpha_{\text{out}}(p) = \max(\alpha'(p),\; \alpha_{\text{floor}} \cdot \alpha_0(p))
\] [15]

Interior band: unchanged. Outside band: unchanged.

### Why LIPC Avoids OSA/BAR Failures

- **No remap, no broadening.** LIPC is a pure multiplicative correction. It cannot widen the transition zone because it only reduces alpha, never moves it spatially.
- **Not weak at low alpha.** Unlike BAR's reaction term (which is \(\sim \alpha(1-\alpha)\) → near zero when \(\alpha \approx 0\)), the inverse-premultiply test is *strongest* at low alpha, because that's where \(\hat{F}\) diverges most from true foreground if alpha is too high. A pixel with \(\alpha = 0.1\) on a white background where true foreground is dark will yield \(\hat{F} \approx\) white, producing a high halo score.
- **Geometry-aware.** Acts only on the exterior band; the \(\max(\phi,0)\) constraint is implicit in \(E_{\text{out}}\).
- **No temporal side effects.** Purely local, frame-by-frame computation on post-EMA alpha. Does not modify the EMA state.

***

## Overlay Branch: Contour-Hierarchy Hole Carving (CHHC)

### Diagnosis

The overlay failure is topological: the pipeline treats the entire frame as foreground. The center-hole flood breakthrough works but has two remaining weaknesses:

1. **Chat holes** — not always reachable from simple rectangular seeds if the overlay geometry is irregular.
2. **Leak-through** — flood-fill on a thresholded alpha0 can leak through narrow dark-frame regions if they happen to have low alpha.

### Core Idea

Replace pure flood-fill with a two-stage approach:

**Stage 1: Connected-component hole detection via contour hierarchy.** Threshold the raw alpha0, find contours with `cv2.RETR_CCOMP` (two-level hierarchy), and identify interior holes as contours whose parent is the outermost frame contour. This is topology-correct by construction — holes are defined by the frame boundary, not by seed geometry.[16][17]

**Stage 2: Size-gated + position-gated hole selection.** Accept a hole only if it meets minimum area (to reject tiny texture gaps in the frame) and centroid falls within expected gameplay/chat regions (to reject gaps between frame decorations).

### Mathematical Formulation

Let:

- \(M_{\text{raw}}(p) = [\alpha_0(p) > T_\alpha]\) — binary foreground mask, threshold \(T_\alpha\)
- Apply `cv2.morphologyEx(CLOSE, k)` with small kernel \(k = 3\)–5 px to seal compression gaps in the frame
- \(\{C_i, H_i\}\) — contours and hierarchy from `cv2.findContours(M_{\text{raw}}, RETR_CCOMP, CHAIN_APPROX_SIMPLE)`
- For hierarchy entry \(H_i = [\text{next}, \text{prev}, \text{child}, \text{parent}]\):
  - Outer frame = contour \(i\) where \(H_i[3] = -1\) (no parent) with largest area
  - Holes = contours \(j\) where \(H_j[3] = i_{\text{frame}}\) (parent is the outer frame)

**Hole acceptance criteria:**

\[
\text{accept}(j) = [\text{area}(C_j) > A_{\min}] \;\land\; [\text{centroid}(C_j) \in \mathcal{R}_{\text{valid}}]
\] [18]

where \(A_{\min}\) is the minimum hole area (e.g., 5% of frame area) and \(\mathcal{R}_{\text{valid}}\) is a generous region excluding only extreme edges (e.g., within 90% of frame dimensions, centered).

**Frame mask construction:**

\[
M_{\text{holes}}(p) = \bigcup_{j \in \text{accepted}} \text{fillPoly}(C_j)
\] [19]

\[
M_{\text{frame}}(p) = M_{\text{raw}}(p) \;\land\; \neg M_{\text{holes}}(p)
\] [20]

**Edge feathering:**

\[
d(p) = \text{cv2.distanceTransform}(M_{\text{frame}}, \text{L2})
\] [21]

\[
\alpha_{\text{overlay}}(p) = \begin{cases} 1.0 & d(p) > r_{\text{hard}} \\ d(p) / r_{\text{hard}} & 0 < d(p) \le r_{\text{hard}} \\ 0.0 & d(p) = 0 \;\land\; \neg M_{\text{frame}}(p) \end{cases}
\] [22]

with \(r_{\text{hard}} \approx 2\)–3 px for a crisp OBS-ready feather.

### Why CHHC Is Better Than Pure Flood-Fill

- **Topology-correct.** Contour hierarchy explicitly models parent-child relationships; holes are children of the frame contour, not connected-to-seed regions. This naturally handles irregularly shaped holes.[17][23]
- **No seed geometry assumptions.** No need to guess center-rect or chat-rect; the algorithm finds holes from the mask topology itself.
- **No leak-through risk.** The `CLOSE` morphology operation seals narrow gaps in the frame before contour extraction. Holes are defined as *enclosed* regions, so they cannot leak through to the outside.
- **Size + position gating.** Tiny decorative gaps (holes in armor, texture noise) are rejected by the area threshold. Edge-of-frame holes (frame border artifacts) are rejected by the centroid constraint.

***

## Shared Pieces

Both modes share:

- Background color estimation: median of \(\alpha_0 < 0.05\) pixels in RGB space.
- Morphological close with small kernel for cleanup.
- Final `np.clip(alpha, 0, 1)`.
- Config loading and batch runner infrastructure.

***

## Insertion Points

### alpha_fix_2/config.py

```python
# --- Mode selection ---
mode: Literal["subject", "overlay"] = "subject"

# --- SUBJECT: LIPC parameters ---
lipc_enabled: bool = True
lipc_alpha_min: float = 0.02       # skip near-zero pixels
lipc_t_delta: float = 0.35         # fg-bg color distance threshold
lipc_t_luma: float = 0.80          # fg luma threshold
lipc_sigma_d: float = 2.5          # distance falloff (px)
lipc_lambda: float = 0.65          # clamp strength
lipc_band_radius: int = 6          # exterior band width

# --- OVERLAY: CHHC parameters ---
chhc_enabled: bool = True
chhc_t_alpha: float = 0.12         # binary threshold for raw mask
chhc_close_kernel: int = 5         # morphological close kernel size
chhc_min_hole_frac: float = 0.03   # minimum hole area as fraction of frame
chhc_valid_margin: float = 0.05    # centroid must be this far from frame edge (fraction)
chhc_feather_r: float = 2.5        # feather radius (px)
```

### alpha_fix_2/pipeline.py

Inside `_segment_frame`, after the existing EMA + cleanup block:

```python
if self.config.mode == "subject" and self.config.lipc_enabled:
    alpha = self._apply_lipc(alpha, alpha0, frame_bgr,
                             self._signed_distance, self._confidence,
                             self.config)
elif self.config.mode == "overlay" and self.config.chhc_enabled:
    alpha = self._apply_chhc(alpha0, frame_bgr, self.config)
```

For overlay mode, CHHC replaces the entire post-anchor refinement chain (EMA, OSA, BAR, etc. are irrelevant for overlay topology).

## Pseudocode: LIPC (Subject)

```python
def _apply_lipc(self, alpha, alpha0, frame_bgr, phi, conf, cfg):
    frame = frame_bgr.astype(np.float32) / 255.0
    H, W = alpha.shape

    # Background color estimate
    bg_mask = alpha0 < 0.05
    if np.count_nonzero(bg_mask) > 100:
        bg = np.median(frame[bg_mask], axis=0)
    else:
        bg = np.array([1.0, 1.0, 1.0], dtype=np.float32)

    # Exterior band
    ext = (phi > 0) & (phi <= cfg.lipc_band_radius)
    active = ext & (alpha > cfg.lipc_alpha_min)

    if not np.any(active):
        return alpha

    # Inverse-premultiply: estimate foreground
    a_safe = np.maximum(alpha, cfg.lipc_alpha_min)
    F_hat = (frame - (1.0 - a_safe)[..., None] * bg[None, None, :]) / a_safe[..., None]
    F_hat = np.clip(F_hat, 0.0, 2.0)

    # Foreground luma
    Y_F = 0.2126 * F_hat[...,0] + 0.7152 * F_hat[...,1] + 0.0722 * F_hat[...,2]

    # Foreground-background distance
    delta_F = np.linalg.norm(F_hat - bg[None,None,:], axis=-1)

    # Halo score
    h_color = np.clip((cfg.lipc_t_delta - delta_F) / cfg.lipc_t_delta, 0, 1)
    h_luma  = np.clip((Y_F - cfg.lipc_t_luma) / (1.0 - cfg.lipc_t_luma + 1e-8), 0, 1)
    h = h_color * h_luma

    # Distance weight (phi > 0 in exterior)
    w = np.exp(-0.5 * (phi / cfg.lipc_sigma_d) ** 2)

    # Alpha reduction
    reduction = cfg.lipc_lambda * h * w * conf
    alpha_new = alpha.copy()
    alpha_new[active] *= (1.0 - np.clip(reduction[active], 0, 1))

    # Floor
    alpha_new = np.maximum(alpha_new, cfg.cnvm_tlp_alpha_floor * alpha0)
    return np.clip(alpha_new, 0, 1)
```

## Pseudocode: CHHC (Overlay)

```python
def _apply_chhc(self, alpha0, frame_bgr, cfg):
    H, W = alpha0.shape

    # Step 1: Binary mask + morphological close
    m_raw = (alpha0 > cfg.chhc_t_alpha).astype(np.uint8) * 255
    kernel = cv2.getStructuringElement(
        cv2.MORPH_ELLIPSE, (cfg.chhc_close_kernel, cfg.chhc_close_kernel))
    m_closed = cv2.morphologyEx(m_raw, cv2.MORPH_CLOSE, kernel)

    # Step 2: Contour hierarchy
    contours, hierarchy = cv2.findContours(
        m_closed, cv2.RETR_CCOMP, cv2.CHAIN_APPROX_SIMPLE)

    if hierarchy is None or len(contours) == 0:
        return alpha0  # fallback: return raw

    hierarchy = hierarchy[0]
    frame_area = H * W

    # Find outermost frame contour (no parent, largest area)
    frame_idx = -1
    max_area = 0
    for i, h in enumerate(hierarchy):
        if h[3] == -1:  # no parent
            a = cv2.contourArea(contours[i])
            if a > max_area:
                max_area = a
                frame_idx = i

    if frame_idx == -1:
        return alpha0

    # Step 3: Find holes (children of frame contour)
    holes = []
    min_area = cfg.chhc_min_hole_frac * frame_area
    margin_x = cfg.chhc_valid_margin * W
    margin_y = cfg.chhc_valid_margin * H

    for i, h in enumerate(hierarchy):
        if h[3] == frame_idx:  # parent is the frame
            area = cv2.contourArea(contours[i])
            if area < min_area:
                continue
            M = cv2.moments(contours[i])
            if M["m00"] < 1:
                continue
            cx = M["m10"] / M["m00"]
            cy = M["m01"] / M["m00"]
            if margin_x < cx < W - margin_x and margin_y < cy < H - margin_y:
                holes.append(i)

    # Step 4: Build hole mask
    m_holes = np.zeros((H, W), dtype=np.uint8)
    for idx in holes:
        cv2.drawContours(m_holes, contours, idx, 255, cv2.FILLED)

    # Step 5: Frame mask = closed raw minus holes
    m_frame = (m_closed > 0) & (m_holes == 0)

    # Step 6: Feathered alpha
    dist_inside = cv2.distanceTransform(
        m_frame.astype(np.uint8) * 255, cv2.DIST_L2, 3)

    alpha_ov = np.zeros((H, W), dtype=np.float32)
    alpha_ov[dist_inside > cfg.chhc_feather_r] = 1.0
    feather_zone = (dist_inside > 0) & (dist_inside <= cfg.chhc_feather_r)
    alpha_ov[feather_zone] = dist_inside[feather_zone] / cfg.chhc_feather_r

    return np.clip(alpha_ov, 0, 1)
```

| P71 | lipc_gentle | 0.40 | 0.40 | 0.85 | 3.0 | 6 | Conservative: test mechanism is active |
| P72 | lipc_target | 0.65 | 0.35 | 0.80 | 2.5 | 6 | Primary target parameters |
| P73 | lipc_strong | 0.85 | 0.30 | 0.75 | 2.0 | 8 | Aggressive: find thinning threshold |
| P74 | lipc_fixed_bg | 0.65 | 0.35 | 0.80 | 2.5 | 6 | Same as P72 but force bg=[9][9][9] |

Metrics to track: outer_band_mass, transition_band_mass, temporal_jitter, temporal_lag_support, core_mean_alpha, soft_edge_fraction, **bright_outer_mass** (new: sum of alpha where \(\phi > 0\), band, \(\hat{F}\) luma > 0.85, \(\Delta_F < 0.25\)).

## Automatic Failure Metrics

### Subject Mode

| Metric | Formula | Pass Gate | Warn Gate | Fail Gate |
|--------|---------|-----------|-----------|-----------|
| Halo reduction | bright_outer_mass vs baseline | ≤ 0.90× baseline | ≤ 0.95× | > 1.0× (worse) |
| Core thinning | core_mean_alpha | ≥ 0.9920 | ≥ 0.9910 | < 0.9900 |
| Ramp broadening | transition_band_mass | ≤ baseline + 0.002 | ≤ baseline + 0.004 | > baseline + 0.005 |
| Temporal lag | temporal_lag_support | ≤ baseline + 0.005 | ≤ baseline + 0.010 | > baseline + 0.015 |
| Edge collapse | soft_edge_fraction | ≥ baseline − 0.008 | ≥ baseline − 0.012 | < baseline − 0.015 |

### Overlay Mode

| Metric | Formula | Pass Gate | Warn Gate | Fail Gate |
|--------|---------|-----------|-----------|-----------|
| Center hole | center_mean_alpha | ≤ 0.03 | ≤ 0.05 | > 0.10 |
| Frame preserved | frame_mean_alpha | ≥ 0.97 | ≥ 0.95 | < 0.90 |
| Global fill | global_nonzero_frac | ≤ 0.35 | ≤ 0.40 | > 0.50 |
| Hole count | num_holes_detected | ≥ 1 | ≥ 1 | 0 (no holes found) |
| Leakage | false_hole_frac (holes outside valid region) | 0 | ≤ 0.01 | > 0.02 |

***

## Verdict, Backup, and Falsification

**Code next: OVERLAY CHHC.** The overlay branch addresses the most catastrophic user-facing failure (OBS display capture completely hidden, 99.99% nonzero). CHHC is low-risk (morphology + contours + area filtering — all standard OpenCV primitives), topology-correct by construction, and directly generalizes the proven center-hole flood success. Implementation: ~40 lines of core logic, ~30 minutes.[17]

**Backup: SUBJECT LIPC.** Implement immediately after CHHC. LIPC is the first subject-mode proposal that attacks the *color-contamination root cause* instead of the alpha-profile shape. It directly uses the inverse compositing equation to detect halo pixels, which is orthogonal to everything OSA/BAR tried. ~35 lines of core logic, ~30 minutes.[8][7]

**Falsification criterion for LIPC:** If, after P73 (lipc_strong: \(\lambda = 0.85\), \(T_\Delta = 0.30\), \(T_Y = 0.75\), \(\sigma_d = 2.0\), \(R_s = 8\)), bright_outer_mass is not reduced by at least 15% relative to baseline AND soft_edge_fraction drops below baseline − 0.012, then the white-halo alpha excess is NOT caused by background-colored foreground estimates, and the root cause is upstream (anchor matte or LAB distance computation assigns alpha to background pixels regardless of color signal). In that case, pause all post-EMA subject refinements and investigate the anchor construction stage.
